=
google_ads;




if(google_ads.length
!=
0)
{








apply_ad_config(google_ads.length);









render_ads(true,
window['ad_config_top']);









if(window['backfillParam'])
{












window['backfillParam']['pl_rnum']
=
google_ads.length;












window['backfillParam']['pl_time']
=
Date.now()
-
afc_ad_start_time;








}




}
}

function
apply_ad_config(num)
{
window['ad_config_top']
=
Math.min(2,
num);
window['ad_config_bot']
=
Math.min(2,
num);
}

google_ad_client
=
'ca-aj-cat';
google_ad_channel
=
'cx_ask_wiki,ad_dirN';
google_ad_output
=
'js';
google_max_num_ads
=
'4';
google_ad_type
=
'text';
google_image_size
=
'';
google_num_ads_recieved=
'';
google_language
=
'';
google_country
=
'';
google_encoding
=
'utf8';
google_safe
=
'medium';
google_adtest
=
'off';
google_ad_section
=
'default';
google_page_url
=
'';
google_hints
=
'Aerosmith';
google_kw
=
'';
google_kw_type
=
'broad';


var
backfillParam
=
{




pl_rqnum
:
google_max_num_ads,




pl_hints
:
google_hints,




pl_rp
:
"false",




pl_kw
:
google_kw,




pl_cl
:
google_ad_client,




pl_ch
:
google_ad_channel,




pl_hex
:
"#FDFEEE",




pl_type
:
"afc",




pl_clksp
:
"none"};

var
word_arr
;

var
word_arr_len
;


function
highlightQuery(input_str)
{

var
queryTokenArray
=
"aerosmith,";


var
tok_arr
=
queryTokenArray.split(",");

for(tok_arr_idx=0;
tok_arr_idx
<
tok_arr.length-1;
tok_arr_idx
++)
{

if(isCombinationWord(tok_arr[tok_arr_idx])){
word_arr
=
tok_arr[tok_arr_idx].split("-");
word_arr_len
=
word_arr.length;
first_pos
=
input_str.toLowerCase().indexOf(word_arr[0],0);

if(first_pos
!=-1)
{
input_str
=
highlightCombinationWords(input_str,first_pos);
}
}
else
{
first_pos
=
input_str.toLowerCase().indexOf(tok_arr[tok_arr_idx],0);
if(first_pos
!=
-1
&&
tok_arr[tok_arr_idx].length
>
0)
{
input_str
=
highlightSimpleWords(input_str,tok_arr[tok_arr_idx],first_pos);
}
}
}
return
input_str;
}

function
isCombinationWord(word){
if(word.indexOf("-")
!=
-1){
return
true;
}
else
{
return
false;
}
}


function
isAlpha(ch)
{
if
(ch
!=
null
&&
ch.match(/^[a-zA-Z0-9]+$/)){
return
true;
}
return
false;
}

function
isQueryinInput(firstindex,
input_str,
j){
for(i=firstindex;
i<
input_str.length
;
++i)
{
var
currindex
=
i;

if(!isAlpha(input_str.charAt(i)))
{
if(firstindex
==
currindex)

{
firstindex++;
}
else
{
if(word_arr[j]
!=
input_str.substring(firstindex,currindex).toLowerCase())
return
-1;
if
(j
==
word_arr_len-1)
return
currindex;
else
return
isQueryinInput(currindex+1,input_str,++j);
}
}
}

if(j
<
word_arr_len)
{
if(word_arr[j]
!=
input_str.substring(firstindex,currindex+1).toLowerCase())
return
-1;
}

return
(currindex
+
1)
;
}


function

highlightCombinationWords(input_str,first_pos)
{
exactmatch
=
isQueryinInput(first_pos+word_arr[0].length,input_str,1)
;
if(exactmatch
!=-1
)

{
bold_str
=
"<b>"
+
input_str.substring(first_pos,exactmatch)
+
"</b>";
input_str
=
input_str.substring(0,first_pos)
+
bold_str
+
input_str.substring(exactmatch);
next_pos
=
input_str.toLowerCase().indexOf(word_arr[0],exactmatch+7);
while(next_pos
!=
-1)
{
return
highlightCombinationWords(input_str,next_pos);
}
}
return
input_str;
}


function

highlightSimpleWords(input_str,token,
first_pos)
{
var
end_pos
=
first_pos
+
token.length;
if(!isAlpha(input_str.charAt(end_pos))
&&
!isAlpha(input_str.charAt(first_pos-1))){
bold_str
=
"<b>"
+
input_str.substring(first_pos,end_pos)
+
"</b>";
input_str
=
input_str.substring(0,first_pos)
+
bold_str
+
input_str.substring(end_pos);
next_pos
=
input_str.toLowerCase().indexOf(token,end_pos+7);
}
else
{
next_pos
=
input_str.toLowerCase().indexOf(token,end_pos);
}

while(next_pos
!=
-1)
{
return
highlightSimpleWords(input_str,token,next_pos);
}
return
input_str;
}</script>

<p><b>Aerosmith</b>
is
an
American
<a
href="/wiki/Hard_rock?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Hard
rock">hard
rock</a>
band,
sometimes
referred
to
as
&quot;The
Bad
Boys
from
Boston&quot;<sup
id="cite_ref-4"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-4"><span>[</span>4<span>]</span></a></sup>
and
&quot;America's
Greatest
Rock
and
Roll
Band.&quot;<sup
id="cite_ref-Walker_20_5-0"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-Walker_20-5"><span>[</span>5<span>]</span></a></sup><sup
id="cite_ref-mtv.com_6-0"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-mtv.com-6"><span>[</span>6<span>]</span></a></sup><sup
id="cite_ref-NewHampshire_7-0"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-NewHampshire-7"><span>[</span>7<span>]</span></a></sup><sup
id="cite_ref-Mieses_B.05_8-0"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-Mieses_B.05-8"><span>[</span>8<span>]</span></a></sup>
Their
style,
which
is
rooted
in
<a
href="/wiki/Blues?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Blues">blues</a>-based
<a
href="/wiki/Hard_rock?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Hard
rock">hard
rock</a>,<sup
id="cite_ref-allmusic_9-0"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-allmusic-9"><span>[</span>9<span>]</span></a></sup><sup
id="cite_ref-Aerosmith:_Biography:_Rolling_Stone_10-0"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-Aerosmith:_Biography:_Rolling_Stone-10"><span>[</span>10<span>]</span></a></sup>
has
come
to
also
incorporate
elements
of
<a
href="/wiki/Pop_music?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Pop
music">pop</a>,<sup
id="cite_ref-11"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-11"><span>[</span>11<span>]</span></a></sup>
<a
href="/wiki/Heavy_metal_music?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Heavy
metal
music">heavy
metal</a>,<sup
id="cite_ref-allmusic_9-1"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-allmusic-9"><span>[</span>9<span>]</span></a></sup>
and
<a
href="/wiki/Rhythm_and_blues?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Rhythm
and
blues">rhythm
and
blues</a>,<sup
id="cite_ref-Aerosmith:_Get_A_Grip:_Music_Reviews:_Rolling_Stone_12-0"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-Aerosmith:_Get_A_Grip:_Music_Reviews:_Rolling_Stone-12"><span>[</span>12<span>]</span></a></sup>
and
has
inspired
many
subsequent
rock
artists.<sup
id="cite_ref-Allmusic_-_Pop-metal_13-0"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-Allmusic_-_Pop-metal-13"><span>[</span>13<span>]</span></a></sup>
The
band
was
formed
in
Boston
Massachusetts
in
1970.
Guitarist
<a
href="/wiki/Joe_Perry_(musician)?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Joe
Perry
(musician)">Joe
Perry</a>
and
bassist
<a
href="/wiki/Tom_Hamilton_(musician)?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Tom
Hamilton
(musician)">Tom
Hamilton</a>,
originally
in
a
band
together
called
the
Jam
Band,
met
up
with
vocalist/harmonica
player
<a
href="/wiki/Steven_Tyler?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Steven
Tyler">Steven
Tyler</a>,
drummer
<a
href="/wiki/Joey_Kramer?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Joey
Kramer">Joey
Kramer</a>,
and
guitarist
<a
href="/wiki/Ray_Tabano?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Ray
Tabano">Ray
Tabano</a>,
and
formed
Aerosmith.
In
1971,
Tabano
was
replaced
by
<a
href="/wiki/Brad_Whitford?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Brad
Whitford">Brad
Whitford</a>,
and
the
band
began
developing
a
following
in
Boston.</p>








<p>They
were
signed
to
<a
href="/wiki/Columbia_Records?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Columbia
Records">Columbia
Records</a>
in
1972,
and
released
a
string
of
multi-platinum
albums,
beginning
with
their
1973
<a
href="/wiki/Aerosmith_(album)?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Aerosmith
(album)">eponymous
debut
album</a>,
followed
by
their
1974
album
<i><a
href="/wiki/Get_Your_Wings?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Get
Your
Wings">Get
Your
Wings</a></i>.
In
1975,
the
band
broke
into
the
mainstream
with
the
album
<i><a
href="/wiki/Toys_in_the_Attic_(album)?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Toys
in
the
Attic
(album)">Toys
in
the
Attic</a></i>,
and
their
1976
follow-up
<i><a
href="/wiki/Rocks_(album)?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Rocks
(album)"
class="mw-redirect">Rocks</a></i>
cemented
their
status
as
hard
rock
superstars.<sup
id="cite_ref-14"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-14"><span>[</span>14<span>]</span></a></sup>
Two
additional
albums
followed
in
1977
and
1979.
Throughout
the
1970s,
the
band
toured
extensively
and
charted
a
string
of
Hot
100
singles.
By
the
end
of
the
decade,
they
were
among
the
most
popular
hard
rock
bands
in
the
world
and
developed
a
loyal
following
of
fans,
often
referred
to
as
the
&quot;<a
href="/wiki/Blue_Army_(Aerosmith)?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Blue
Army
(Aerosmith)">Blue
Army</a>&quot;.<sup
id="cite_ref-autogenerated1_15-0"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-autogenerated1-15"><span>[</span>15<span>]</span></a></sup>
However,
<a
href="/wiki/Drug_addiction?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Drug
addiction"
class="mw-redirect">drug
addiction</a>
and
internal
conflict
took
their
toll
on
the
band,
which
resulted
in
the
departures
of
Perry
and
Whitford
in
1979
and
1981,
respectively;
they
were
replaced
by
<a
href="/wiki/Jimmy_Crespo?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Jimmy
Crespo">Jimmy
Crespo</a>
and
<a
href="/wiki/Rick_Dufay?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Rick
Dufay">Rick
Dufay</a>.<sup
id="cite_ref-Aerosmith:_Biography:_Rolling_Stone_10-1"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-Aerosmith:_Biography:_Rolling_Stone-10"><span>[</span>10<span>]</span></a></sup>
The
band
did
not
fare
well
between
1980
and
1984,
releasing
a
lone
album,
<i><a
href="/wiki/Rock_in_a_Hard_Place?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Rock
in
a
Hard
Place">Rock
in
a
Hard
Place</a></i>,
which
went
gold
but
failed
to
match
their
previous
successes.</p>








<p>Perry
and
Whitford
returned
in
1984
and
the
band
signed
a
new
deal
with
<a
href="/wiki/Geffen_Records?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Geffen
Records">Geffen
Records</a>.
After
a
comeback
tour,
the
band
recorded
<i><a
href="/wiki/Done_with_Mirrors?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Done
with
Mirrors">Done
with
Mirrors</a></i>
(1985),
which
won
some
critical
praise
but
failed
to
come
close
to
commercial
expectations.
It
was
not
until
the
band's
collaboration
with
rap
group
<a
href="/wiki/Run%E2%80%93D.M.C.?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Runâ€“D.M.C.">Runâ€“D.M.C.</a>
in
1986,
and
the
1987
release
<i><a
href="/wiki/Permanent_Vacation_(album)?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Permanent
Vacation
(album)">Permanent
Vacation</a></i>,
that
they
regained
the
level
of
popularity
they
had
experienced
in
the
1970s.<sup
id="cite_ref-16"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-16"><span>[</span>16<span>]</span></a></sup>
Throughout
the
late
1980s
and
1990s,
the
band
scored
several
hits
and
won
numerous
awards
for
music
from
the
multi-platinum
albums
<i><a
href="/wiki/Pump_(album)?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Pump
(album)">Pump</a></i>
(1989),
<i><a
href="/wiki/Get_a_Grip?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Get
a
Grip">Get
a
Grip</a></i>
(1993),
and
<i><a
href="/wiki/Nine_Lives_(Aerosmith_album)?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Nine
Lives
(Aerosmith
album)">Nine
Lives</a></i>
(1997),
and
embarked
on
their
most
extensive
concert
tours
to
date.
The
band
also
became
a
pop
culture
phenomenon
with
popular
music
videos
and
notable
appearances
in
television,
film,
and
video
games.
Their
comeback
has
been
described
as
one
of
the
most
remarkable
and
spectacular
in
rock
'n'
roll
history.<sup
id="cite_ref-allmusic_9-2"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-allmusic-9"><span>[</span>9<span>]</span></a></sup><sup
id="cite_ref-Aerosmith:_Biography:_Rolling_Stone_10-2"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-Aerosmith:_Biography:_Rolling_Stone-10"><span>[</span>10<span>]</span></a></sup>
Additional
albums
followed
in
2001
and
2004.
The
band
toured
throughout
the
2000s,
touring
every
year
except
2008.
After
44
years
of
performing,
the
band
continues
to
tour
and
record
music.
Their
latest
album,
<i><a
href="/wiki/Music_from_Another_Dimension!?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Music
from
Another
Dimension!">Music
from
Another
Dimension!</a></i>,
was
released
on
November
6,
2012.</p>








<p>Aerosmith
is
<a
href="/wiki/List_of_best-selling_music_artists?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="List
of
best-selling
music
artists">the
best-selling
American
rock
band
of
all
time</a>,
having
sold
more
than
150
million
albums
worldwide,<sup
id="cite_ref-17"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-17"><span>[</span>17<span>]</span></a></sup>
including
70.2
million
albums
in
the
United
States
alone.<sup
id="cite_ref-RIAA.C2.A0.E2.80.94_Top_Selling_Artists_18-0"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-RIAA.C2.A0.E2.80.94_Top_Selling_Artists-18"><span>[</span>18<span>]</span></a></sup>
They
also
hold
the
record
for
the
most
<a
href="/wiki/RIAA_certification?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="RIAA
certification">gold</a>
albums
by
an
American
group
and
are
tied
for
the
most
<a
href="/wiki/RIAA_certification?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="RIAA
certification">multi-platinum</a>
albums
by
an
American
group.
The
band
has
scored
21
<a
href="/wiki/Top_40?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Top
40">Top
40</a>
hits
on
the
<a
href="/wiki/Billboard_Hot_100?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Billboard
Hot
100"><i>Billboard</i>
Hot
100</a>,
nine
number-one
<a
href="/wiki/Mainstream_Rock_Tracks?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Mainstream
Rock
Tracks"
class="mw-redirect">Mainstream
Rock</a>
hits,
four
<a
href="/wiki/Grammy_Award?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Grammy
Award">Grammy
Awards</a>,
and
ten
<a
href="/wiki/MTV_Video_Music_Awards?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="MTV
Video
Music
Awards"
class="mw-redirect">MTV
Video
Music
Awards</a>.
They
were
inducted
into
the
<a
href="/wiki/Rock_and_Roll_Hall_of_Fame?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Rock
and
Roll
Hall
of
Fame">Rock
and
Roll
Hall
of
Fame</a>
in
2001,
and
were
included
among
both
<i>Rolling
Stone'</i>s
and
VH1's
lists
of
the
100
Greatest
Artists
of
All
Time.<sup
id="cite_ref-19"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-19"><span>[</span>19<span>]</span></a></sup></p>

<h2><span
class="mw-headline"
id="History">History</span>
<span
class="mw-editsection">[<a
href="/wiki?title=Aerosmith&amp;action=edit&amp;section=1"
title="Edit
section:
History">edit</a>]</span></h2>








<h3><span
class="mw-headline"
id="Formation_.281964.E2.80.931971.29">Formation
(1964â€“1971)</span>
<span
class="mw-editsection">[<a
href="/wiki?title=Aerosmith&amp;action=edit&amp;section=2"
title="Edit
section:
Formation
(1964â€“1971)">edit</a>]</span></h3>








<p>In
1964,
<a
href="/wiki/Steven_Tyler?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Steven
Tyler">Steven
Tyler</a>
formed
his
own
band
called
The
Strangeursâ€”later
Chain
Reactionâ€”
in
<a
href="/wiki/New_Hampshire?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="New
Hampshire">New
Hampshire</a>.
Meanwhile,
Perry
and
Hamilton
formed
the
Jam
Band
(commonly
known
as
&quot;Joe
Perry's
Jam
Band&quot;),
which
was
based
on
free-form
and
blues.
Hamilton
and
Perry
moved
to
Boston,
Massachusetts
in
September.<sup
id="cite_ref-20"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-20"><span>[</span>20<span>]</span></a></sup>
There
they
met
<a
href="/wiki/Joey_Kramer?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Joey
Kramer">Joey
Kramer</a>,
a
drummer
from
Yonkers,
New
York.
Kramer
knew
Tyler
and
had
always
hoped
to
play
in
a
band
with
him.<sup
id="cite_ref-Walk_This_Way.2C_page_104_21-0"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-Walk_This_Way.2C_page_104-21"><span>[</span>21<span>]</span></a></sup>
Kramer,
a
<a
href="/wiki/Berklee_College_of_Music?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Berklee
College
of
Music">Berklee
College
of
Music</a>
student,
decided
to
quit
school
to
join
Jam
Band.<sup
id="cite_ref-Walk_This_Way.2C_page_104_21-1"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-Walk_This_Way.2C_page_104-21"><span>[</span>21<span>]</span></a></sup>
In
1970,
Chain
Reaction
and
Jam
Band
played
at
the
same
gig.
Tyler
immediately
loved
Jam
Band's
sound,
and
wanted
to
combine
the
two
bands.
In
October
1970,
the
bands
met
up
again
and
considered
the
proposition.
Tyler,
who
had
been
a
drummer
and
backup
singer
in
Chain
Reaction,
adamantly
refused
to
play
drums
in
this
new
band,
insisting
he
would
only
take
part
if
he
could
be
the
frontman
and
lead
vocalist.<sup
id="cite_ref-Walk_This_Way.2C_page_104_21-2"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-Walk_This_Way.2C_page_104-21"><span>[</span>21<span>]</span></a></sup>
The
others
agreed,
and
a
new
band
was
born.
The
band
moved
into
a
home
together
at
1325
Commonwealth
Avenue
in
<a
href="/wiki/Boston?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Boston">Boston</a>,
where
they
wrote
and
rehearsed
music
together
and
relaxed
in
between
shows.<sup
id="cite_ref-22"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-22"><span>[</span>22<span>]</span></a></sup></p>








<p>The
members
of
the
band
reportedly
spent
afternoons
getting
stoned
and
watching
<i><a
href="/wiki/Three_Stooges?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Three
Stooges"
class="mw-redirect">Three
Stooges</a></i>
reruns.<sup
id="cite_ref-Davis.2C_pp._106.E2.80.93107_23-0"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-Davis.2C_pp._106.E2.80.93107-23"><span>[</span>23<span>]</span></a></sup>
One
day,
they
had
a
post-Stooges
meeting
to
try
to
come
up
with
a
name.
Kramer
said
when
he
was
in
school
he
would
write
the
word
aerosmith
all
over
his
notebooks.<sup
id="cite_ref-Davis.2C_pp._106.E2.80.93107_23-1"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-Davis.2C_pp._106.E2.80.93107-23"><span>[</span>23<span>]</span></a></sup>
The
name
had
popped
into
his
head
after
listening
to
<a
href="/wiki/Harry_Nilsson?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Harry
Nilsson">Harry
Nilsson</a>'s
album
<i><a
href="/wiki/Aerial_Ballet?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Aerial
Ballet">Aerial
Ballet</a></i>,
which
featured
jacket
art
of
a
circus
performer
jumping
out
of
a
biplane.
Initially,
Kramer's
bandmates
were
nonplussed;
they
all
thought
he
was
referring
to
<a
href="/wiki/Arrowsmith_(novel)?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Arrowsmith
(novel)">the
Sinclair
Lewis
novel</a>
they
were
required
to
read
in
high
school
English
class.
&quot;No,
not
Arrowsmith,&quot;
Kramer
explained.
&quot;A-E-R-O...Aerosmith.&quot;<sup
id="cite_ref-24"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-24"><span>[</span>24<span>]</span></a></sup>
The
band
settled
upon
this
name
after
also
considering
&quot;The
Hookers&quot;
and
&quot;Spike
Jones.&quot;<sup
id="cite_ref-Davis.2C_pp._106.E2.80.93107_23-2"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-Davis.2C_pp._106.E2.80.93107-23"><span>[</span>23<span>]</span></a></sup><sup
id="cite_ref-mtv_25-0"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-mtv-25"><span>[</span>25<span>]</span></a></sup></p>








<p>Soon,
the
band
hired
<a
href="/wiki/Ray_Tabano?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Ray
Tabano">Ray
Tabano</a>,
a
childhood
friend
of
Tyler,
as
rhythm
guitarist
and
began
playing
local
shows.<sup
id="cite_ref-26"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-26"><span>[</span>26<span>]</span></a></sup>
Aerosmith
played
their
first
gig
in
<a
href="/wiki/Mendon,_Massachusetts?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Mendon,
Massachusetts">Mendon,
Massachusetts</a>
at
<a
href="/wiki/Nipmuc_Regional_High_School?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Nipmuc
Regional
High
School">Nipmuc
Regional
High
School</a>
(now
Miscoe
Hill
Middle
School)
on
November
6,
1970.
In
1971,
Tabano
was
replaced
by
<a
href="/wiki/Brad_Whitford?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Brad
Whitford">Brad
Whitford</a>,
who
also
attended
the
Berklee
School
of
Music
and
was
formerly
of
the
band
<a
href="/wiki/Earth_Inc.?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Earth
Inc."
class="mw-redirect">Earth
Inc.</a><sup
id="cite_ref-27"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-27"><span>[</span>27<span>]</span></a></sup>
Whitford,
being
from
<a
href="/wiki/Reading,_Massachusetts?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Reading,
Massachusetts">Reading,
Massachusetts</a>,
had
played
at
Reading's
<a
href="/wiki/Coolidge_Middle_School_(Reading,_Massachusetts)?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Coolidge
Middle
School
(Reading,
Massachusetts)">AW
Coolidge
Middle
School</a>.
Other
than
a
period
from
July
1979
to
April
1984,
the
line-up
of
Tyler,
Perry,
Hamilton,
Kramer,
and
Whitford
has
stayed
the
same.</p>








<h3><span
class="mw-headline"
id="Record_deal.2C_Aerosmith.2C_Get_Your_Wings_and_Toys_in_the_Attic_.281971.E2.80.931975.29">Record
deal,
<i>Aerosmith</i>,
<i>Get
Your
Wings</i>
and
<i>Toys
in
the
Attic</i>
(1971â€“1975)</span>
<span
class="mw-editsection">[<a
href="/wiki?title=Aerosmith&amp;action=edit&amp;section=3"
title="Edit
section:
Record
deal,
Aerosmith,
Get
Your
Wings
and
Toys
in
the
Attic
(1971â€“1975)">edit</a>]</span></h3>

colspan="2"
class="mbox-text"
style="line-height:1.1em;"><span
style="font-size:smaller;"><i>Problems
playing

help</a>.</i></span></td>

<p>After
forming
the
band
and
finalizing
the
lineup
in
1971,
the
band
started
to
garner
some
local
success
doing
live
shows.<sup
id="cite_ref-Aerosmith:_Biography:_Rolling_Stone_10-3"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-Aerosmith:_Biography:_Rolling_Stone-10"><span>[</span>10<span>]</span></a></sup>
Originally
booked
through
the
Ed
Malhoit
Agency,<sup
id="cite_ref-28"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-28"><span>[</span>28<span>]</span></a></sup>
the
band
signed
a
promotion
deal
with
Frank
Connelly
and
eventually
secured
a
management
deal
with
David
Krebs
and
Steve
Leber
in
1972.<sup
id="cite_ref-29"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-29"><span>[</span>29<span>]</span></a></sup>
Krebs
and
Leber
invited
<a
href="/wiki/Columbia_Records?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Columbia
Records">Columbia
Records</a>
President
<a
href="/wiki/Clive_Davis?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Clive
Davis">Clive
Davis</a>
to
see
the
band
at
<a
href="/wiki/Max%27s_Kansas_City?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Max's
Kansas
City">Max's
Kansas
City</a>
in
New
York
City.
Aerosmith
was
not
originally
scheduled
to
play
that
night
at
the
club,
but
they
paid
from
their
own
pockets
to
secure
a
place
on
the
bill,
reportedly
the
only
band
ever
to
do
so
at
Max's.
&quot;<a
href="/wiki/No_Surprize?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="No
Surprize"
class="mw-redirect">No
Surprize</a>&quot;
off
their
<i><a
href="/wiki/Night_in_the_Ruts?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Night
in
the
Ruts">Night
in
the
Ruts</a></i>
album
celebrates
the
moment
their
fame
began.<sup
id="cite_ref-30"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-30"><span>[</span>30<span>]</span></a></sup></p>








<p>Aerosmith
signed
with
Columbia
in
mid-1972
for
a
reported
$125,000
and
issued
their
debut
album,
<i><a
href="/wiki/Aerosmith_(album)?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Aerosmith
(album)">Aerosmith</a></i>.<sup
id="cite_ref-31"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-31"><span>[</span>31<span>]</span></a></sup>
Released
in
January
1973,
the
album
peaked
at
number
166.<sup
id="cite_ref-allmusic_9-3"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-allmusic-9"><span>[</span>9<span>]</span></a></sup>
The
album
was
straightforward
rock
and
roll
with
well-defined
blues
influences,
laying
the
groundwork
for
Aerosmith's
signature
<a
href="/wiki/Blues-rock?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Blues-rock"
class="mw-redirect">blues-rock</a>
sound.<sup
id="cite_ref-STE_32-0"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-STE-32"><span>[</span>32<span>]</span></a></sup>
Although
the
highest-charting
single
from
the
album
was
&quot;<a
href="/wiki/Dream_On_(Aerosmith_song)?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Dream
On
(Aerosmith
song)">Dream
On</a>&quot;
at
number
59,<sup
id="cite_ref-33"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-33"><span>[</span>33<span>]</span></a></sup>
several
tracks
(such
as
&quot;<a
href="/wiki/Mama_Kin?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Mama
Kin">Mama
Kin</a>&quot;
and
&quot;Walkin'
the
Dog&quot;)
would
become
staples
of
the
band's
live
shows
and
receive
airplay
on
rock
radio.<sup
id="cite_ref-34"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-34"><span>[</span>34<span>]</span></a></sup>
The
album
reached
gold
status
initially,
eventually
went
on
to
sell
two
million
copies,
and
was
certified
double
platinum
after
the
band
reached
mainstream
success
over
a
decade
later.<sup
id="cite_ref-RIAA.C2.A0.E2.80.94_Searchable_Database_35-0"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-RIAA.C2.A0.E2.80.94_Searchable_Database-35"><span>[</span>35<span>]</span></a></sup>
After
constant
touring,
the
band
released
their
second
album
<i><a
href="/wiki/Get_Your_Wings?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Get
Your
Wings">Get
Your
Wings</a></i>
in
1974,
the
first
of
a
string
of
multi-platinum
albums
produced
by
<a
href="/wiki/Jack_Douglas_(record_producer)?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Jack
Douglas
(record
producer)">Jack
Douglas</a>.<sup
id="cite_ref-36"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-36"><span>[</span>36<span>]</span></a></sup>
This
album
included
the
rock
radio
hits
&quot;<a
href="/wiki/Same_Old_Song_and_Dance?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Same
Old
Song
and
Dance">Same
Old
Song
and
Dance</a>&quot;
and
&quot;<a
href="/wiki/Train_Kept_A-Rollin%27?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Train
Kept
A-Rollin'">Train
Kept
A-Rollin'</a>&quot;,
a
cover
done
previously
by
<a
href="/wiki/The_Yardbirds?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="The
Yardbirds">The
Yardbirds</a>.<sup
id="cite_ref-37"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-37"><span>[</span>37<span>]</span></a></sup>
The
album
also
contained
several
fan
favorites
including
&quot;<a
href="/wiki/Lord_of_the_Thighs?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Lord
of
the
Thighs">Lord
of
the
Thighs</a>&quot;,
&quot;<a
href="/wiki/Seasons_of_Wither?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Seasons
of
Wither">Seasons
of
Wither</a>&quot;,
and
&quot;<a
href="/wiki/S.O.S._(Too_Bad)?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="S.O.S.
(Too
Bad)">S.O.S.
(Too
Bad)</a>&quot;,
darker
songs
which
have
become
staples
in
the
band's
live
shows.<sup
id="cite_ref-38"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-38"><span>[</span>38<span>]</span></a></sup>
To
date,
<i>Get
Your
Wings</i>
has
sold
three
million
copies.<sup
id="cite_ref-RIAA.C2.A0.E2.80.94_Searchable_Database_35-1"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-RIAA.C2.A0.E2.80.94_Searchable_Database-35"><span>[</span>35<span>]</span></a></sup></p>








<p>It
was
1975's
<i><a
href="/wiki/Toys_in_the_Attic_(album)?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Toys
in
the
Attic
(album)">Toys
in
the
Attic</a></i>,
however,
that
established
Aerosmith
as
international
stars
competing
with
the
likes
of
<a
href="/wiki/Led_Zeppelin?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Led
Zeppelin">Led
Zeppelin</a>
and
<a
href="/wiki/The_Rolling_Stones?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="The
Rolling
Stones">The
Rolling
Stones</a>.<sup
id="cite_ref-autogenerated1_15-1"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-autogenerated1-15"><span>[</span>15<span>]</span></a></sup>
Originally
derided
as
Rolling
Stones
knockoffs
in
part
due
to
the
physical
resemblance
between
lead
singers
Steven
Tyler
and
<a
href="/wiki/Mick_Jagger?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Mick
Jagger">Mick
Jagger</a>,<sup
id="cite_ref-Aerosmith:_Biography:_Rolling_Stone_10-4"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-Aerosmith:_Biography:_Rolling_Stone-10"><span>[</span>10<span>]</span></a></sup>
<i>Toys
in
the
Attic</i>
showed
that
Aerosmith
was
a
unique
and
talented
band
in
their
own
right.<sup
id="cite_ref-Toys_in_the_Attic_Review_39-0"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-Toys_in_the_Attic_Review-39"><span>[</span>39<span>]</span></a></sup>
<i>Toys
in
the
Attic</i>
was
an
immediate
success,
starting
with
the
single
&quot;<a
href="/wiki/Sweet_Emotion?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Sweet
Emotion">Sweet
Emotion</a>&quot;,
which
became
the
band's
first
<a
href="/wiki/Top_40?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Top
40">Top
40</a>
hit.<sup
id="cite_ref-40"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-40"><span>[</span>40<span>]</span></a></sup>
This
was
followed
by
a
successful
re-release
of
&quot;<a
href="/wiki/Dream_On_(Aerosmith_song)?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Dream
On
(Aerosmith
song)">Dream
On</a>&quot;
which
hit
number
6,
becoming
their
best
charting
single
of
the
1970s.<sup
id="cite_ref-41"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-41"><span>[</span>41<span>]</span></a></sup>
&quot;<a
href="/wiki/Walk_This_Way?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Walk
This
Way">Walk
This
Way</a>&quot;,
re-released
in
1976,
reached
the
Top
10
in
early
1977.<sup
id="cite_ref-Aerosmith:_Biography:_Rolling_Stone_10-5"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-Aerosmith:_Biography:_Rolling_Stone-10"><span>[</span>10<span>]</span></a></sup></p>








<p>In
addition,
&quot;<a
href="/wiki/Toys_in_the_Attic_(song)?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Toys
in
the
Attic
(song)">Toys
in
the
Attic</a>&quot;
and
&quot;Big
Ten
Inch
Record&quot;
(a
song
originally
recorded
by
<a
href="/wiki/Bull_Moose_Jackson?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Bull
Moose
Jackson">Bull
Moose
Jackson</a>)
became
concert
staples.<sup
id="cite_ref-42"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-42"><span>[</span>42<span>]</span></a></sup>
As
a
result
of
this
success,
both
of
the
band's
previous
albums
re-charted.<sup
id="cite_ref-43"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-43"><span>[</span>43<span>]</span></a></sup>
<i>Toys
in
the
Attic</i>
has
gone
on
to
become
the
band's
bestselling
studio
album
in
the
States,
with
certified
U.S.
sales
of
eight
million
copies.<sup
id="cite_ref-RIAA.C2.A0.E2.80.94_Searchable_Database_35-2"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-RIAA.C2.A0.E2.80.94_Searchable_Database-35"><span>[</span>35<span>]</span></a></sup>
The
band
toured
in
support
of
<i>Toys
in
the
Attic</i>,
where
they
started
to
get
more
recognition.<sup
id="cite_ref-autogenerated1_15-2"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-autogenerated1-15"><span>[</span>15<span>]</span></a></sup>
Also
around
this
time,
the
band
established
their
home
base
as
&quot;<a
href="/wiki/Wherehouse?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Wherehouse">The
Wherehouse</a>&quot;
in
<a
href="/wiki/Waltham,_Massachusetts?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Waltham,
Massachusetts">Waltham,
Massachusetts</a>,
where
they
would
record
and
rehearse
music,
as
well
as
conduct
business.<sup
id="cite_ref-44"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-44"><span>[</span>44<span>]</span></a></sup></p>

class="mw-headline"

the

<i>Live!

and

<div
class="thumbcaption">











<div

Steven
Tyler
and
Joe
Perry
performing
live
in
concert.

</div>








<p>Aerosmith's
next
album
was
1976's
<i><a
href="/wiki/Rocks_(album)?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Rocks
(album)"
class="mw-redirect">Rocks</a>,</i>
which
&quot;captured
Aerosmith
at
their
most
raw
and
rocking&quot;.<sup
id="cite_ref-Rocks_Review_45-0"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-Rocks_Review-45"><span>[</span>45<span>]</span></a></sup>
It
went
<a
href="/wiki/Gold_record?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Gold
record"
class="mw-redirect">platinum</a>
swiftly<sup
id="cite_ref-RIAA.C2.A0.E2.80.94_Searchable_Database_35-3"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-RIAA.C2.A0.E2.80.94_Searchable_Database-35"><span>[</span>35<span>]</span></a></sup>
and
featured
two
<a
href="/wiki/FM_broadcasting?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="FM
broadcasting">FM</a>
hits,
&quot;<a
href="/wiki/Last_Child?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Last
Child">Last
Child</a>&quot;
and
&quot;<a
href="/wiki/Back_in_the_Saddle?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Back
in
the
Saddle">Back
in
the
Saddle</a>&quot;,
as
well
as
the
ballad
&quot;<a
href="/wiki/Home_Tonight?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Home
Tonight">Home
Tonight</a>&quot;,
which
also
charted.<sup
id="cite_ref-Aerosmith_Chart_Positions_46-0"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-Aerosmith_Chart_Positions-46"><span>[</span>46<span>]</span></a></sup>
<i>Rocks</i>
has
sold
four
million
copies
to
date.<sup
id="cite_ref-RIAA.C2.A0.E2.80.94_Searchable_Database_35-4"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-RIAA.C2.A0.E2.80.94_Searchable_Database-35"><span>[</span>35<span>]</span></a></sup>
Both
<i>Toys
in
the
Attic</i>
and
<i>Rocks</i>
are
highly
regarded,<sup
id="cite_ref-Toys_in_the_Attic_Review_39-1"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-Toys_in_the_Attic_Review-39"><span>[</span>39<span>]</span></a></sup><sup
id="cite_ref-Rocks_Review_45-1"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-Rocks_Review-45"><span>[</span>45<span>]</span></a></sup>
especially
in
the
hard
rock
genre,
and
appear
on
such
lists
as
<i>Rolling
Stone'</i>s
<a
href="/wiki/500_Greatest_Albums_of_All_Time?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="500
Greatest
Albums
of
All
Time"
class="mw-redirect">500
Greatest
Albums
of
All
Time</a>,<sup
id="cite_ref-47"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-47"><span>[</span>47<span>]</span></a></sup><sup
id="cite_ref-48"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-48"><span>[</span>48<span>]</span></a></sup>
and
are
cited
by
members
of
<a
href="/wiki/Guns_N%27_Roses?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Guns
N'
Roses">Guns
N'
Roses</a>,
<a
href="/wiki/Metallica?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Metallica">Metallica</a>,
and
<a
href="/wiki/M%C3%B6tley_Cr%C3%BCe?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="M&ouml;tley
Cr&uuml;e">M&ouml;tley
Cr&uuml;e</a>
as
having
large
influences
on
their
music.<sup
id="cite_ref-49"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-49"><span>[</span>49<span>]</span></a></sup><sup
id="cite_ref-50"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-50"><span>[</span>50<span>]</span></a></sup>
Kurt
Cobain
listed
<i>Rocks</i>
as
one
of
the
albums
he
thought
were
most
influential
to
Nirvana's
sound
in
his
journal
in
1993.<sup
id="cite_ref-joyfulnoiserecordings.com_51-0"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-joyfulnoiserecordings.com-51"><span>[</span>51<span>]</span></a></sup>
Soon
after
<i><a
href="/wiki/Rocks_(album)?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Rocks
(album)"
class="mw-redirect">Rocks</a></i>
was
released,
the
band
continued
to
tour
heavily,
this
time
headlining
their
own
shows
and
playing
to
several
large
stadiums
and
rock
festivals.<sup
id="cite_ref-Aerosmith:_Biography:_Rolling_Stone_10-6"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-Aerosmith:_Biography:_Rolling_Stone-10"><span>[</span>10<span>]</span></a></sup></p>








<p>Aerosmith's
next
album
was
1977's
<i><a
href="/wiki/Draw_the_Line_(Aerosmith_album)?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Draw
the
Line
(Aerosmith
album)">Draw
the
Line</a></i>.
The
album's
recording
was
affected
by
the
excesses
of
the
band
members,
but
the
record
still
had
memorable
moments.<sup
id="cite_ref-Aerosmith_Chart_Positions_46-1"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-Aerosmith_Chart_Positions-46"><span>[</span>46<span>]</span></a></sup>
The
<a
href="/wiki/Draw_the_Line_(song)?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Draw
the
Line
(song)">title
track</a>
charted
just
shy
of
the
Top
40
and
remains
a
live
staple,
and
&quot;<a
href="/wiki/Kings_and_Queens_(Aerosmith_song)?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Kings
and
Queens
(Aerosmith
song)">Kings
and
Queens</a>&quot;
also
charted.<sup
id="cite_ref-Aerosmith_Chart_Positions_46-2"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-Aerosmith_Chart_Positions-46"><span>[</span>46<span>]</span></a></sup>
The
album
went
on
to
sell
2
million
copies.<sup
id="cite_ref-RIAA.C2.A0.E2.80.94_Searchable_Database_35-5"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-RIAA.C2.A0.E2.80.94_Searchable_Database-35"><span>[</span>35<span>]</span></a></sup>
The
band
toured
extensively
in
support
of
the
album,
however
<a
href="/wiki/Drug_abuse?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Drug
abuse"
class="mw-redirect">drug
abuse</a>
and
the
fast-paced
life
of
touring
and
recording
began
affecting
their
performances.
Lead
singer
Steven
Tyler
and
lead
guitarist
Joe
Perry
became
known
as
&quot;<a
href="/wiki/The_Toxic_Twins?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="The
Toxic
Twins"
class="mw-redirect">The
Toxic
Twins</a>&quot;
because
of
their
notorious
abuse
of
drugs
on
and
off
the
stage.<sup
id="cite_ref-Aerosmith:_Biography:_Rolling_Stone_10-7"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-Aerosmith:_Biography:_Rolling_Stone-10"><span>[</span>10<span>]</span></a></sup><sup
id="cite_ref-rockhall_52-0"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-rockhall-52"><span>[</span>52<span>]</span></a></sup>
While
continuing
to
tour
and
record
into
the
late
1970s,
Aerosmith
acted
in
the
movie
version
of
<i><a
href="/wiki/Sgt._Pepper%27s_Lonely_Hearts_Club_Band_(film)?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Sgt.
Pepper's
Lonely
Hearts
Club
Band
(film)">Sgt.
Pepper's
Lonely
Hearts
Club
Band</a></i>.<sup
id="cite_ref-allmusic_9-4"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-allmusic-9"><span>[</span>9<span>]</span></a></sup>
Their
cover
of
the
<a
href="/wiki/The_Beatles?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="The
Beatles">Beatles</a>
hit
&quot;<a
href="/wiki/Come_Together?qsrc=3044#Covers"
title="Come
Together">Come
Together</a>&quot;
was
included
in
the
album's
soundtrack
and
would
be
the
band's
last
Top
40
hit
for
nearly
10
years.<sup
id="cite_ref-Aerosmith_Chart_Positions_46-3"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-Aerosmith_Chart_Positions-46"><span>[</span>46<span>]</span></a></sup>
The
live
release
<i><a
href="/wiki/Live!_Bootleg?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Live!
Bootleg">Live!
Bootleg</a></i>,
originally
released
as
a
double
album,
was
put
out
in
1978
and
captured
the
band's
rawness<sup
id="cite_ref-53"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-53"><span>[</span>53<span>]</span></a></sup>
during
the
heyday
of
the
Draw
the
Line
tour.
The
stand-alone
single
&quot;<a
href="/wiki/Chip_Away_the_Stone?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Chip
Away
the
Stone">Chip
Away
the
Stone</a>&quot;
was
also
released
in
1978
and
charted
at
number
77.</p>








<h3><span
class="mw-headline"
id="Departures_of_Perry_and_Whitford.2C_Night_in_the_Ruts_and_Rock_in_a_Hard_Place_.281979.E2.80.931984.29">Departures
of
Perry
and
Whitford,
<i>Night
in
the
Ruts</i>
and
<i>Rock
in
a
Hard
Place</i>
(1979â€“1984)</span>
<span
class="mw-editsection">[<a
href="/wiki?title=Aerosmith&amp;action=edit&amp;section=5"
title="Edit
section:
Departures
of
Perry
and
Whitford,
Night
in
the
Ruts
and
Rock
in
a
Hard
Place
(1979â€“1984)">edit</a>]</span></h3>








<p>In
1979,
the
band
started
work
on
their
next
album,
<i><a
href="/wiki/Night_in_the_Ruts?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Night
in
the
Ruts">Night
in
the
Ruts</a></i>.
Aerosmith
decided
to
go
on
tour
during
a
break
in
the
recording
schedule
but
tensions
within
the
band
were
slowly
coming
to
a
head.
The
band's
touring
schedule
brought
them
to
<a
href="/wiki/Cleveland_Stadium?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Cleveland
Stadium">Cleveland
Stadium</a>
on
July
28,
1979,
where
they
headlined
the
<a
href="/wiki/World_Series_of_Rock?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="World
Series
of
Rock">World
Series
of
Rock</a>
festival.
In
a
heated
argument
backstage,
Joe
Perry's
wife,
Elissa,
threw
a
glass
of
milk
at
Tom
Hamilton's
wife,
Terry.
Following
the
show,
Tyler
and
Perry
got
into
a
heated
argument
when
Tyler
confronted
Perry
about
his
wife's
antics,
and
after
the
course
of
the
argument
Perry
quit
the
band
and
left
(while
Tyler
claims
in
his
autobiography
that
he
fired
Perry
from
the
band).
In
leaving,
Perry
took
some
of
the
music
that
he
had
written
with
him.
Shortly
after
his
departure
Perry
formed
a
new
band
called
<a
href="/wiki/The_Joe_Perry_Project?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="The
Joe
Perry
Project">The
Joe
Perry
Project</a>.<sup
id="cite_ref-allmusic_9-5"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-allmusic-9"><span>[</span>9<span>]</span></a></sup><sup
id="cite_ref-Aerosmith:_Biography:_Rolling_Stone_10-8"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-Aerosmith:_Biography:_Rolling_Stone-10"><span>[</span>10<span>]</span></a></sup></p>








<p>Since
there
was
still
work
to
be
done
on
<i>Night
in
the
Ruts</i>,
Aerosmith
needed
fill-in
musicians
to
take
Perry's
place
on
the
songs
that
needed
to
be
recorded
to
complete
the
album.
Rhythm
guitarist
Brad
Whitford
took
over
some
of
the
lead
parts
and
<a
href="/wiki/Richard_Supa?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Richard
Supa">Richie
Supa</a>,
the
band's
longtime
writing
partner,
filled
in
where
needed
until
the
band
was
able
to
hire
<a
href="/wiki/Jimmy_Crespo?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Jimmy
Crespo">Jimmy
Crespo</a>
to
take
over
as
the
full-time
guitarist.
<i>Night
in
the
Ruts</i>
was
released
in
November
1979,
but
only
managed
to
sell
enough
records
to
be
certified
Gold
at
the
time
(it
would
eventually
sell
enough
to
be
Platinum
certified
in
1994).
The
only
single
the
album
spawned,
a
cover
of
&quot;<a
href="/wiki/Remember_(Walking_in_the_Sand)?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Remember
(Walking
in
the
Sand)">Remember
(Walking
in
the
Sand)</a>&quot;
by
the
Shangri-Las,
peaked
at
#67
on
the
Billboard
Hot
100.<sup
id="cite_ref-Aerosmith_Chart_Positions_46-4"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-Aerosmith_Chart_Positions-46"><span>[</span>46<span>]</span></a></sup></p>








<p>The
tour
for
<i>Night
in
the
Ruts</i>
commenced
shortly
thereafter
but
the
band
found
themselves
playing
in
smaller
and
smaller
venues
than
they
were
before
due
to
their
popularity
beginning
to
wane.
Steven
Tyler's
drug
issues
were
starting
to
affect
his
performance
and
songwriting,
and
he
reached
bottom
when
he
collapsed
on
stage
during
a
show
in
<a
href="/wiki/Portland,_Maine?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Portland,
Maine">Portland,
Maine</a>
in
1980
and
did
not
get
up
for
the
remainder
of
the
set.<sup
id="cite_ref-54"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-54"><span>[</span>54<span>]</span></a></sup>
Also
in
1980,
Aerosmith
released
its
<i><a
href="/wiki/Greatest_Hits_(Aerosmith_album)?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Greatest
Hits
(Aerosmith
album)">Greatest
Hits</a></i>
album.
While
the
compilation
didn't
chart
very
high
initially,
it
gained
popularity
later
and
has
gone
on
to
become
the
band's
bestselling
album
in
the
United
States,
with
sales
of
11
million
copies.<sup
id="cite_ref-RIAA.C2.A0.E2.80.94_Searchable_Database_35-6"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-RIAA.C2.A0.E2.80.94_Searchable_Database-35"><span>[</span>35<span>]</span></a></sup>
In
the
fall
of
1980,
Tyler
was
injured
in
a
serious
motorcycle
accident,
which
left
him
hospitalized
for
two
months,
and
unable
to
tour
or
record
well
into
1981.<sup
id="cite_ref-55"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-55"><span>[</span>55<span>]</span></a></sup></p>








<p>In
1981,
Aerosmith
began
work
on
their
next
album,
which
was
titled
<i><a
href="/wiki/Rock_in_a_Hard_Place?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Rock
in
a
Hard
Place">Rock
in
a
Hard
Place</a></i>
and
saw
them
reunite
with
producer
Jack
Douglas.
Once
again,
though,
they
would
be
forced
to
deal
with
another
departure.
After
the
first
song
for
the
album,
&quot;<a
href="/wiki/Lightning_Strikes_(Aerosmith_song)?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Lightning
Strikes
(Aerosmith
song)">Lightning
Strikes</a>&quot;,
was
recorded
Brad
Whitford
departed
the
band
and
decided
to
form
a
duo
with
<a
href="/wiki/Derek_St._Holmes?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Derek
St.
Holmes">Derek
St.
Holmes</a>,
with
whom
he
recorded
a
<a
href="/wiki/Whitford/St._Holmes?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Whitford/St.
Holmes">self-titled
album</a>
that
failed
to
garner
much
interest.
Whitford
later
joined
up
with
The
Joe
Perry
Project
and
played
with
them
in
1984.<sup
id="cite_ref-56"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-56"><span>[</span>56<span>]</span></a></sup></p>








<p>With
<a
href="/wiki/Rick_Dufay?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Rick
Dufay">Rick
Dufay</a>
taking
Whitford's
place,
<i>Rock
in
a
Hard
Place</i>
was
released
on
August
1,
1982.<sup
id="cite_ref-57"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-57"><span>[</span>57<span>]</span></a></sup>
The
album
was
not
well
received
and
only
reached
#32
on
the
Billboard
200
album
chart.<sup
id="cite_ref-RIAA.C2.A0.E2.80.94_Searchable_Database_35-7"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-RIAA.C2.A0.E2.80.94_Searchable_Database-35"><span>[</span>35<span>]</span></a></sup>
Only
one
single
charted,
the
aforementioned
&quot;Lightning
Strikes&quot;,
which
peaked
at
number
21
on
the
<i>Billboard</i>
<a
href="/wiki/Hot_Mainstream_Rock_Tracks?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Hot
Mainstream
Rock
Tracks">Top
Tracks</a>
chart.<sup
id="cite_ref-Aerosmith_Chart_Positions_46-5"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-Aerosmith_Chart_Positions-46"><span>[</span>46<span>]</span></a></sup>
As
with
the
tour
for
<i>Night
in
the
Ruts</i>,
Aerosmith
was
unable
to
book
larger
venues
and
instead
had
to
rely
on
filling
clubs
and
theaters,
which
they
struggled
to
do.
At
a
show
in
<a
href="/wiki/Worcester,_Massachusetts?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Worcester,
Massachusetts">Worcester,
Massachusetts</a>,
Tyler
and
Perry
reunited
and
got
high
backstage
before
the
show.
Tyler
was
so
intoxicated
that
he
collapsed
on
stage
again
and
like
before
could
not
get
up.<sup
id="cite_ref-58"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-58"><span>[</span>58<span>]</span></a></sup></p>








<p>On
February
14,
1984,
Perry
and
Whitford
saw
Aerosmith
perform
at
Boston's
<a
href="/wiki/Orpheum_Theatre_(Boston)?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Orpheum
Theatre
(Boston)">Orpheum
Theater</a>.
Shortly
thereafter,
discussions
began
to
reintegrate
the
two
into
the
band
and
several
months
later,
the
original
members
of
Aerosmith
reunited.<sup
id="cite_ref-59"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-59"><span>[</span>59<span>]</span></a></sup>
Steven
Tyler
recalls:</p>








<table
class="cquote"
style="margin:auto;
border-collapse:

<td

should

the

all
five
of
us
got
together
in
the
same
room
for
the
first
time
again.
We
all
started
laughin'â€”it

the

years
had
never
passed.
We

we'd

the
right
move.</td>

<sup

</td>

<h3><span
class="mw-headline"
id="Back_in_the_Saddle_reunion_tour.2C_Done_with_Mirrors_and_drug_rehab_.281984.E2.80.931986.29">Back
in
the
Saddle
reunion
tour,
<i>Done
with
Mirrors</i>
and
drug
rehab
(1984â€“1986)</span>
<span
class="mw-editsection">[<a
href="/wiki?title=Aerosmith&amp;action=edit&amp;section=6"
title="Edit
section:
Back
in
the
Saddle
reunion
tour,
Done
with
Mirrors
and
drug
rehab
(1984â€“1986)">edit</a>]</span></h3>








<p>In
1984,
Aerosmith
embarked
on
a
reunion
tour
called
the
<i><a
href="/wiki/Back_in_the_Saddle_Tour?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Back
in
the
Saddle
Tour">Back
in
the
Saddle
Tour</a></i>,<sup
id="cite_ref-allmusic_9-6"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-allmusic-9"><span>[</span>9<span>]</span></a></sup>
which
led
to
the
live
album
<i><a
href="/wiki/Classics_Live_II?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Classics
Live
II"
class="mw-redirect">Classics
Live
II</a></i>.
While
concerts
on
the
tour
were
well-attended,
it
was
plagued
with
several
incidents,
mostly
attributed
to
drug
abuse
by
band
members.<sup
id="cite_ref-allmusic_9-7"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-allmusic-9"><span>[</span>9<span>]</span></a></sup>
Their
problems
still
not
behind
them,
the
group
was
signed
to
<a
href="/wiki/Geffen_Records?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Geffen
Records">Geffen
Records</a>
and
began
working
on
a
comeback.<sup
id="cite_ref-Biography.com_61-0"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-Biography.com-61"><span>[</span>61<span>]</span></a></sup>
Despite
the
band
signing
on
to
a
new
record
company,
the
band's
old
label
<a
href="/wiki/Columbia_Records?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Columbia
Records">Columbia</a>
continued
to
reap
the
benefits
of
Aerosmith's
comeback,
releasing
the
live
companion
albums
<i><a
href="/wiki/Classics_Live_I_and_II?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Classics
Live
I
and
II">Classics
Live
I
and
II</a></i>
and
the
collection
<i><a
href="/wiki/Gems_(Aerosmith_album)?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Gems
(Aerosmith
album)">Gems</a></i>.<sup
id="cite_ref-62"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-62"><span>[</span>62<span>]</span></a></sup></p>








<p>In
1985,
the
band
released
the
album
<i><a
href="/wiki/Done_with_Mirrors?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Done
with
Mirrors">Done
with
Mirrors</a></i>,
their
first
studio
album
since
reuniting.
While
the
album
did
receive
some
positive
reviews,<sup
id="cite_ref-63"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-63"><span>[</span>63<span>]</span></a></sup>
it
only
went
gold<sup
id="cite_ref-RIAA.C2.A0.E2.80.94_Searchable_Database_35-8"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-RIAA.C2.A0.E2.80.94_Searchable_Database-35"><span>[</span>35<span>]</span></a></sup>
and
failed
to
produce
a
hit
single
or
generate
any
widespread
interest.<sup
id="cite_ref-Aerosmith_Chart_Positions_46-6"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-Aerosmith_Chart_Positions-46"><span>[</span>46<span>]</span></a></sup>
The
album's
most
notable
track,
&quot;<a
href="/wiki/Let_the_Music_Do_the_Talking_(song)?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Let
the
Music
Do
the
Talking
(song)">Let
the
Music
Do
the
Talking</a>&quot;,
was
in
fact
a
cover
of
a
song
originally
recorded
by
The
Joe
Perry
Project
and
released
on
that
band's
album
of
the
same
name.<sup
id="cite_ref-64"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-64"><span>[</span>64<span>]</span></a></sup>
Nevertheless,
the
band
became
a
popular
concert
attraction
once
again,
<a
href="/wiki/Done_with_Mirrors_Tour?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Done
with
Mirrors
Tour">touring
in
support
of
<i>Done
With
Mirrors</i></a>,
well
into
1986.<sup
id="cite_ref-65"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-65"><span>[</span>65<span>]</span></a></sup>
In
1986,
Tyler
and
Perry
appeared
on
<a
href="/wiki/Run%E2%80%93D.M.C.?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Runâ€“D.M.C.">Runâ€“D.M.C.</a>'s
cover
of
&quot;<a
href="/wiki/Walk_This_Way?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Walk
This
Way">Walk
This
Way</a>&quot;,
a
track
<a
href="/wiki/Rap_rock?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Rap
rock">blending
rock
and
roll
with
hip
hop</a>.<sup
id="cite_ref-mtv_25-1"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-mtv-25"><span>[</span>25<span>]</span></a></sup>
In
reaching
number
4
on
the
<i>Billboard</i>
Hot
100,<sup
id="cite_ref-Rock_on_the_Net_66-0"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-Rock_on_the_Net-66"><span>[</span>66<span>]</span></a></sup>
the
song
and
its
frequently-aired
video
confirmed
rap's
mainstream
appeal
and
resurrected
Aerosmith's
career
by
introducing
the
band's
music
to
a
new
generation.<sup
id="cite_ref-Biography.com_61-1"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-Biography.com-61"><span>[</span>61<span>]</span></a></sup></p>








<p>Yet
the
band
members'
drug
problems
still
stood
in
their
way.
In
1986,
Tyler
completed
a
successful
<a
href="/wiki/Drug_rehabilitation?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Drug
rehabilitation">drug
rehabilitation</a>
program,
after
an
intervention
by
his
fellow
band
members,
a
doctor,
and
manager
<a
href="/wiki/Tim_Collins_(manager)?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Tim
Collins
(manager)">Tim
Collins</a>,
who
believed
that
the
band's
future
would
not
be
bright
if
Tyler
did
not
get
treated.
The
rest
of
the
band
members
also
completed
drug
rehab
programs
over
the
course
of
the
next
couple
of
years.
According
to
the
band's
tell-all
autobiography,
Collins
pledged
in
September
1986
he
could
make
Aerosmith
the
biggest
band
in
the
world
by
1990
if
they
all
completed
drug
rehab.<sup
id="cite_ref-67"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-67"><span>[</span>67<span>]</span></a></sup>
Their
next
album
was
crucial
because
of
the
commercial
disappointment
of
<i>Done
With
Mirrors</i>,
and
as
the
band
members
became
clean,
they
worked
hard
to
make
their
next
album
a
success.<sup
id="cite_ref-68"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-68"><span>[</span>68<span>]</span></a></sup></p>








<h3><span
class="mw-headline"
id="Permanent_Vacation_and_Pump_.281987.E2.80.931991.29"><i>Permanent
Vacation</i>
and
<i>Pump</i>
(1987â€“1991)</span>
<span
class="mw-editsection">[<a
href="/wiki?title=Aerosmith&amp;action=edit&amp;section=7"
title="Edit
section:
Permanent
Vacation
and
Pump
(1987â€“1991)">edit</a>]</span></h3>








<p><i><a
href="/wiki/Permanent_Vacation_(album)?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Permanent
Vacation
(album)">Permanent
Vacation</a></i>
was
released
in
September
1987,
becoming
a
major
hit
and
the
band's
bestselling
album
in
over
a
decade
(selling
5
million
copies
in
the
U.S.),<sup
id="cite_ref-RIAA.C2.A0.E2.80.94_Searchable_Database_35-9"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-RIAA.C2.A0.E2.80.94_Searchable_Database-35"><span>[</span>35<span>]</span></a></sup>
with
all
three
of
its
singles
(&quot;<a
href="/wiki/Dude_(Looks_Like_a_Lady)?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Dude
(Looks
Like
a
Lady)">Dude
(Looks
Like
a
Lady)</a>&quot;,
&quot;<a
href="/wiki/Rag_Doll_(Aerosmith_song)?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Rag
Doll
(Aerosmith
song)">Rag
Doll</a>&quot;,
and
&quot;<a
href="/wiki/Angel_(Aerosmith_song)?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Angel
(Aerosmith
song)">Angel</a>&quot;)
reaching
the
Top
20
of
the
<i>Billboard</i>
Hot
100.<sup
id="cite_ref-Aerosmith_Chart_Positions_46-7"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-Aerosmith_Chart_Positions-46"><span>[</span>46<span>]</span></a></sup>
Steven
Tyler
reveals
in
his
autobiography
that
the
album
was
&quot;...the
first
one
we
ever
did
sober.&quot;<sup
id="cite_ref-69"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-69"><span>[</span>69<span>]</span></a></sup>
Part
of
<i>Permanent
Vacation'</i>s
commercial
success
involved
producer
<a
href="/wiki/Bruce_Fairbairn?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Bruce
Fairbairn">Bruce
Fairbairn</a>
whose
production
touches
(such
as
sound
effects
and
high-quality
recording)
added
interest
to
the
album
and
the
use
of
outside
songwriters
such
as
<a
href="/wiki/Desmond_Child?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Desmond
Child">Desmond
Child</a>,
<a
href="/wiki/Jim_Vallance?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Jim
Vallance">Jim
Vallance</a>,
and
<a
href="/wiki/Holly_Knight?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Holly
Knight">Holly
Knight</a>
who
assisted
the
band
with
lyrics.
While
the
group
was
initially
hesitant
to
using
outside
songwriters,
including
Tyler
being
furious
for
Knight
getting
songwriting
credits
for
changing
one
word
(&quot;Rag
Time&quot;
became
&quot;Rag
Doll&quot;),
the
method
paid
off,
as
<i>Permanent
Vacation</i>
became
the
band's
most
successful
album
in
a
decade.
The
group
went
on
<a
href="/wiki/Permanent_Vacation_Tour?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Permanent
Vacation
Tour">a
subsequent
tour</a>
with
labelmates
<a
href="/wiki/Guns_N%27_Roses?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Guns
N'
Roses">Guns
N'
Roses</a>
(who
have
cited
Aerosmith
as
a
major
influence),
which
was
intense
at
times
because
of
Aerosmith's
new
struggle
to
stay
clean
amidst
Guns
N'
Roses'
well-publicized,
rampant
drug
use.<sup
id="cite_ref-70"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-70"><span>[</span>70<span>]</span></a></sup></p>








<table
class="mbox-small-left"
style="border:1px

#aaa;

<p>Aerosmith's
next
album
was
even
more
successful.
<i><a
href="/wiki/Pump_(album)?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Pump
(album)">Pump</a></i>,
released
in
September
1989,
featured
three
Top
Ten
singles:
&quot;<a
href="/wiki/What_It_Takes_(Aerosmith_song)?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="What
It
Takes
(Aerosmith
song)">What
It
Takes</a>&quot;,
&quot;<a
href="/wiki/Janie%27s_Got_a_Gun?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Janie's
Got
a
Gun">Janie's
Got
a
Gun</a>&quot;,
and
&quot;<a
href="/wiki/Love_in_an_Elevator?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Love
in
an
Elevator">Love
in
an
Elevator</a>&quot;,
as
well
as
the
Top
30
&quot;<a
href="/wiki/The_Other_Side_(Aerosmith_song)?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="The
Other
Side
(Aerosmith
song)">The
Other
Side</a>&quot;,<sup
id="cite_ref-Aerosmith_Chart_Positions_46-8"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-Aerosmith_Chart_Positions-46"><span>[</span>46<span>]</span></a></sup>
re-establishing
the
band
as
a
serious
musical
force.<sup
id="cite_ref-71"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-71"><span>[</span>71<span>]</span></a></sup>
<i>Pump</i>
was
a
critical
and
commercial
success,
eventually
selling
7
million
copies,<sup
id="cite_ref-RIAA.C2.A0.E2.80.94_Searchable_Database_35-10"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-RIAA.C2.A0.E2.80.94_Searchable_Database-35"><span>[</span>35<span>]</span></a></sup>
spawning
several
music
videos
that
were
in
regular
rotation
on
MTV,
and
achieving
four-star
ratings
from
major
music
magazines.<sup
id="cite_ref-72"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-72"><span>[</span>72<span>]</span></a></sup>
<i>Pump</i>
ranked
as
the
fourth-bestselling
album
of
1990.<sup
id="cite_ref-73"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-73"><span>[</span>73<span>]</span></a></sup>
The
band
also
won
its
first
<a
href="/wiki/Grammy_Award?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Grammy
Award">Grammy</a>
in
the
category
of
<a
href="/wiki/Best_Rock_Performance_by_a_Duo_or_Group_with_Vocal?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Best
Rock
Performance
by
a
Duo
or
Group
with
Vocal"
class="mw-redirect">Best
Rock
Performance
by
a
Duo
or
Group
with
Vocal</a>,
for
&quot;Janie's
Got
a
Gun&quot;.<sup
id="cite_ref-grammy_74-0"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-grammy-74"><span>[</span>74<span>]</span></a></sup>
In
addition,
the
video
for
&quot;Janie's
Got
a
Gun&quot;
won
two
<a
href="/wiki/MTV_Video_Music_Awards?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="MTV
Video
Music
Awards"
class="mw-redirect">Video
Music
Awards</a>
and
was
ranked
as
one
of
the
100
greatest
videos
of
all
time
by
<i>Rolling
Stone</i>,
MTV,
and
VH1.
Like
<i>Permanent
Vacation</i>,
<i>Pump</i>
was
produced
by
Bruce
Fairbairn,
who
added
production
touches
such
as
instrumental
interludes
that
provided
transitions
between
songs
to
give
the
album
a
more
complete
sound,
as
well
as
The
Margarita
Horns,
who
added
horns
to
tracks
such
as
&quot;Love
in
an
Elevator&quot;
and
&quot;The
Other
Side&quot;.
Rock
critic
<a
href="/wiki/Stephen_Thomas_Erlewine?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Stephen
Thomas
Erlewine">Stephen
Thomas
Erlewine</a>
claimed
that
<i>Pump</i>
&quot;revels
in
[pop
concessions]
without
ever
losing
sight
of
Aerosmith's
dirty
hard
rock
core&quot;,
going
on
to
say
that,
&quot;such
ambition
and
successful
musical
eclectism
make
<i>Pump</i>
rank
with
<i>Toys
in
the
Attic</i>
and
<i>Rocks</i>.&quot;<sup
id="cite_ref-75"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-75"><span>[</span>75<span>]</span></a></sup>
The
recording
process
for
<i>Pump</i>
was
documented
in
the
video
<i><a
href="/wiki/The_Making_of_Pump?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="The
Making
of
Pump">The
Making
of
Pump</a></i>,
which
has
since
been
re-released
as
a
DVD.
The
music
videos
for
the
album's
singles
were
featured
on
the
release
<i><a
href="/wiki/Things_That_Go_Pump_in_the_Night?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Things
That
Go
Pump
in
the
Night">Things
That
Go
Pump
in
the
Night</a></i>,
which
quickly
went
platinum.<sup
id="cite_ref-RIAA.C2.A0.E2.80.94_Searchable_Database_35-11"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-RIAA.C2.A0.E2.80.94_Searchable_Database-35"><span>[</span>35<span>]</span></a></sup></p>

Aerosmith
appear
in
a
&quot;










<a

on

<p>In
support
of
<i>Pump</i>,
the
band
embarked
on
the
12-month
<a
href="/wiki/Pump_Tour?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Pump
Tour">Pump
Tour</a>,
which
lasted
for
most
of
1990.<sup
id="cite_ref-76"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-76"><span>[</span>76<span>]</span></a></sup>
On
February
21,
1990,
the
band
appeared
in
a
&quot;<a
href="/wiki/Wayne%27s_World?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Wayne's
World">Wayne's
World</a>&quot;
sketch
on
<i><a
href="/wiki/Saturday_Night_Live?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Saturday
Night
Live">Saturday
Night
Live</a>,</i>
debating
the
fall
of
communism
and
the
Soviet
Union,
and
performed
their
recent
hits
&quot;<a
href="/wiki/Janie%27s_Got_a_Gun?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Janie's
Got
a
Gun">Janie's
Got
a
Gun</a>&quot;
and
&quot;<a
href="/wiki/Monkey_on_My_Back?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Monkey
on
My
Back">Monkey
on
My
Back</a>&quot;.<sup
id="cite_ref-77"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-77"><span>[</span>77<span>]</span></a></sup>
The
appearance
of
the
band
in
the
&quot;Wayne's
World&quot;
sketch
was
later
ranked
by
<a
href="/wiki/E!?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="E!">E!</a>
as
the
number-one
moment
in
the
history
of
the
program.<sup
id="cite_ref-78"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-78"><span>[</span>78<span>]</span></a></sup>
On
August
11,
1990,
the
band's
performance
on
MTV's
<i><a
href="/wiki/MTV_Unplugged?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="MTV
Unplugged">Unplugged</a></i>
aired.<sup
id="cite_ref-79"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-79"><span>[</span>79<span>]</span></a></sup>
In
October
1990,
the
Pump
Tour
ended,
with
the
band's
first
ever
performances
in
Australia.<sup
id="cite_ref-80"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-80"><span>[</span>80<span>]</span></a></sup>
That
same
year,
the
band
was
also
inducted
to
the
Hollywood
Rock
Walk.<sup
id="cite_ref-Rock_Walk_81-0"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-Rock_Walk-81"><span>[</span>81<span>]</span></a></sup>
In
November
1991,
the
band
appeared
on
<i><a
href="/wiki/The_Simpsons?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="The
Simpsons">The
Simpsons</a></i>
episode
&quot;<a

Moe's">Flaming
Moe's</a>&quot;<sup
id="cite_ref-82"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-82"><span>[</span>82<span>]</span></a></sup>
and
released
a
box
set
titled
<i><a
href="/wiki/Pandora%27s_Box_(album)?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Pandora's
Box
(album)">Pandora's
Box</a></i>.<sup
id="cite_ref-83"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-83"><span>[</span>83<span>]</span></a></sup>

<a

<a

during

and
