<h3><span
class="mw-headline"
id="Get_a_Grip_and_Big_Ones_.281992.E2.80.931995.29"><i>Get
a
Grip</i>
and
<i>Big
Ones</i>
(1992â€“1995)</span>
<span
class="mw-editsection">[<a
href="/wiki?title=Aerosmith&amp;action=edit&amp;section=8"
title="Edit
section:
Get
a
Grip
and
Big
Ones
(1992â€“1995)">edit</a>]</span></h3>








<p>The
band
took
a
brief
break
before
recording
their
follow-up
to
<i>Pump</i>
in
1992.
Despite
significant
shifts
in
mainstream
music
at
the
beginning
of
the
1990s,<sup
id="cite_ref-Aerosmith:_Get_A_Grip:_Music_Reviews:_Rolling_Stone_12-1"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-Aerosmith:_Get_A_Grip:_Music_Reviews:_Rolling_Stone-12"><span>[</span>12<span>]</span></a></sup>
1993's
<i><a
href="/wiki/Get_a_Grip?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Get
a
Grip">Get
a
Grip</a></i>
was
just
as
successful
commercially,
becoming
their
first
album
to
debut
at
number
1<sup
id="cite_ref-Aerosmith_Albums_Chart_Positions_87-0"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-Aerosmith_Albums_Chart_Positions-87"><span>[</span>87<span>]</span></a></sup>
and
racking
up
sales
of
7
million
copies
in
a
two-and-a-half-year
timespan.<sup
id="cite_ref-RIAA.C2.A0.E2.80.94_Searchable_Database_35-12"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-RIAA.C2.A0.E2.80.94_Searchable_Database-35"><span>[</span>35<span>]</span></a></sup>
The
first
singles
were
the
hard
rocking
&quot;<a
href="/wiki/Livin%27_on_the_Edge?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Livin'
on
the
Edge">Livin'
on
the
Edge</a>&quot;
and
&quot;<a
href="/wiki/Eat_the_Rich_(Aerosmith_song)?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Eat
the
Rich
(Aerosmith
song)">Eat
the
Rich</a>&quot;.
Though
many
critics
were
unimpressed
by
the
focus
on
the
subsequent
interchangeable
power-ballads
in
promoting
the
album,<sup
id="cite_ref-Aerosmith:_Get_A_Grip:_Music_Reviews:_Rolling_Stone_12-2"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-Aerosmith:_Get_A_Grip:_Music_Reviews:_Rolling_Stone-12"><span>[</span>12<span>]</span></a></sup>
all
three
(&quot;<a
href="/wiki/Cryin%27?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Cryin'">Cryin'</a>&quot;,
&quot;<a
href="/wiki/Crazy_(Aerosmith_song)?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Crazy
(Aerosmith
song)">Crazy</a>&quot;
and
&quot;<a
href="/wiki/Amazing_(Aerosmith_song)?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Amazing
(Aerosmith
song)">Amazing</a>&quot;)
proved
to
be
huge
successes
on
radio<sup
id="cite_ref-Aerosmith_Chart_Positions_46-9"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-Aerosmith_Chart_Positions-46"><span>[</span>46<span>]</span></a></sup>
and
MTV.<sup
id="cite_ref-Biography.com_61-2"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-Biography.com-61"><span>[</span>61<span>]</span></a></sup>
The
music
videos
featured
then
up-and-coming
actress
<a
href="/wiki/Alicia_Silverstone?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Alicia
Silverstone">Alicia
Silverstone</a>;
her
provocative
performances
earned
her
the
title
of
&quot;the
Aerosmith
chick&quot;<sup
id="cite_ref-88"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-88"><span>[</span>88<span>]</span></a></sup>
for
the
first
half
of
the
decade.
Steven
Tyler's
daughter
<a
href="/wiki/Liv_Tyler?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Liv
Tyler">Liv
Tyler</a>
was
also
featured
in
the
&quot;Crazy&quot;
video.<sup
id="cite_ref-89"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-89"><span>[</span>89<span>]</span></a></sup>
<i>Get
a
Grip</i>
would
go
on
to
sell
more
than
7
million
copies
in
the
U.S.
alone,<sup
id="cite_ref-RIAA.C2.A0.E2.80.94_Searchable_Database_35-13"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-RIAA.C2.A0.E2.80.94_Searchable_Database-35"><span>[</span>35<span>]</span></a></sup>
and
over
20
million
copies
worldwide.<sup
id="cite_ref-90"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-90"><span>[</span>90<span>]</span></a></sup>
The
band
won
two
<a
href="/wiki/Grammy_Award?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Grammy
Award">Grammy
Awards</a>
for
songs
from
this
album
in
the
category
of
<a
href="/wiki/Grammy_Award_for_Best_Rock_Performance_by_a_Duo_or_Group_with_Vocal?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Grammy
Award
for
Best
Rock
Performance
by
a
Duo
or
Group
with
Vocal">Best
Rock
Performance
by
a
Duo
or
Group
with
Vocal</a>:
for
&quot;Livin'
on
the
Edge&quot;
in
1994
and
&quot;Crazy&quot;
in
1995.<sup
id="cite_ref-grammy_74-1"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-grammy-74"><span>[</span>74<span>]</span></a></sup></p>








<p>During
the
making
of
<i>Get
a
Grip</i>,
the
management
and
record
company
brought
in
a
variety
of
professional
songwriting
collaborators
to
help
give
nearly
all
the
songs
on
the
album
more
commercial
appeal,<sup
id="cite_ref-Aerosmith:_Get_A_Grip:_Music_Reviews:_Rolling_Stone_12-3"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-Aerosmith:_Get_A_Grip:_Music_Reviews:_Rolling_Stone-12"><span>[</span>12<span>]</span></a></sup>
a
trend
which
would
continue
until
the
early
2000s.
However,
this
led
to
accusations
of
<a
href="/wiki/Selling_out?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Selling
out">selling
out</a>
that
would
continue
throughout
the
1990s.<sup
id="cite_ref-91"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-91"><span>[</span>91<span>]</span></a></sup>
In
addition
to
Aerosmith's
<a
href="/wiki/Get_a_Grip_Tour?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Get
a
Grip
Tour">grueling
18
month
world
tour</a>
in
support
of
<i>Get
a
Grip</i>,
the
band
also
did
a
number
of
things
to
help
promote
themselves
and
their
album
and
appeal
to
youth
culture,
including
the
appearance
of
the
band
in
the
movie
<i><a
href="/wiki/Wayne%27s_World_2?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Wayne's
World
2">Wayne's
World
2</a></i><sup
id="cite_ref-92"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-92"><span>[</span>92<span>]</span></a></sup>
where
they
performed
two
songs,<sup
id="cite_ref-93"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-93"><span>[</span>93<span>]</span></a></sup>
the
appearance
of
the
band
and
their
music
in
the
video
games
<i><a
href="/wiki/Revolution_X?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Revolution
X">Revolution
X</a></i>
and
<i><a
href="/wiki/Quest_for_Fame?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Quest
for
Fame">Quest
for
Fame</a></i>,<sup
id="cite_ref-94"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-94"><span>[</span>94<span>]</span></a></sup>
performing
at
<a
href="/wiki/Woodstock_%2794?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Woodstock
'94">Woodstock
'94</a>,<sup
id="cite_ref-95"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-95"><span>[</span>95<span>]</span></a></sup>
using
their
song
&quot;<a
href="/wiki/Deuces_Are_Wild?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Deuces
Are
Wild">Deuces
Are
Wild</a>&quot;
in
<i><a
href="/wiki/The_Beavis_and_Butt-head_Experience?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="The
Beavis
and
Butt-head
Experience">The
Beavis
and
Butt-head
Experience</a></i>,<sup
id="cite_ref-96"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-96"><span>[</span>96<span>]</span></a></sup>
and
opening
their
own
club,
The
Mama
Kin
Music
Hall,
in
<a
href="/wiki/Boston,_MA?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Boston,
MA"
class="mw-redirect">Boston,
MA</a>
in
1994.<sup
id="cite_ref-97"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-97"><span>[</span>97<span>]</span></a></sup>
That
same
year
saw
the
release
of
the
band's
compilation
for
<a
href="/wiki/Geffen_Records?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Geffen
Records">Geffen
Records</a>,
entitled
<i><a
href="/wiki/Big_Ones?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Big
Ones">Big
Ones</a></i>
featuring
their
biggest
hits
from
<i>Permanent
Vacation</i>,
<i>Pump</i>,
and
<i>Get
a
Grip</i>,
&quot;Deuces
Are
Wild&quot;
from
the
<i>Beavis
and
Butt-head
Experience</i>,
as
well
as
two
new
songs,
&quot;<a
href="/wiki/Blind_Man?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Blind
Man">Blind
Man</a>&quot;
and
&quot;<a
href="/wiki/Walk_on_Water_(Aerosmith_song)?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Walk
on
Water
(Aerosmith
song)">Walk
on
Water</a>&quot;,<sup
id="cite_ref-98"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-98"><span>[</span>98<span>]</span></a></sup>
both
of
which
experienced
great
success
on

rock
charts.<sup
id="cite_ref-Aerosmith_Chart_Positions_46-10"
class="reference"><a

<p>Aerosmith
had
signed
a
$30
million
contract
with
<a
href="/wiki/Columbia_Records?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Columbia
Records">Columbia
Records</a>/<a
href="/wiki/Sony_Music?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Sony
Music"
class="mw-redirect">Sony
Music</a>
in
1991,
but
had
only
recorded
three
of
their
six
contractual
albums
with
<a
href="/wiki/Geffen_Records?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Geffen
Records">Geffen
Records</a>
at
that
point
(<i>Done
with
Mirrors</i>,
<i>Permanent
Vacation</i>,
and
<i>Pump</i>).
Between
1991
and
1996,
they
released
two
more
albums
with
Geffen
(<i>Get
a
Grip</i>
and
<i>Big
Ones</i>),
which
meant
they
now
had
five
albums
with
Geffen
under
their
belt
(along
with
a
planned
live
compilation),
which
meant
they
could
now
begin
recording
for
their
new
contract
with
Columbia.<sup
id="cite_ref-allmusic_9-8"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-allmusic-9"><span>[</span>9<span>]</span></a></sup><sup
id="cite_ref-99"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-99"><span>[</span>99<span>]</span></a></sup>
The
band
took
time
off
with
their
families
before
working
on
their
next
album,
<i><a
href="/wiki/Nine_Lives_(Aerosmith_album)?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Nine
Lives
(Aerosmith
album)">Nine
Lives</a></i>,
which
was
plagued
with
personnel
problems,
including
the
firing
of
manager
<a
href="/wiki/Tim_Collins_(manager)?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Tim
Collins
(manager)">Tim
Collins</a>,<sup
id="cite_ref-allmusic_9-9"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-allmusic-9"><span>[</span>9<span>]</span></a></sup>
who,
according
to
band
members,
had
nearly
caused
the
band
to
break
up.<sup
id="cite_ref-100"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-100"><span>[</span>100<span>]</span></a></sup>
The
album's
producer
was
also
changed
from
<a
href="/wiki/Glen_Ballard?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Glen
Ballard">Glen
Ballard</a>
to
<a
href="/wiki/Kevin_Shirley?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Kevin
Shirley">Kevin
Shirley</a>.<sup
id="cite_ref-101"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-101"><span>[</span>101<span>]</span></a></sup>
<i>Nine
Lives</i>
was
released
in
March
1997.
Reviews
were
mixed,
and
<i>Nine
Lives</i>
initially
fell
down
the
charts,<sup
id="cite_ref-allmusic_9-10"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-allmusic-9"><span>[</span>9<span>]</span></a></sup>
although
it
had
a
long
chart
life
and
sold
double
platinum
in
the
United
States
alone,<sup
id="cite_ref-RIAA.C2.A0.E2.80.94_Searchable_Database_35-14"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-RIAA.C2.A0.E2.80.94_Searchable_Database-35"><span>[</span>35<span>]</span></a></sup>
fueled
by
its
singles,
&quot;<a
href="/wiki/Falling_in_Love_(Is_Hard_on_the_Knees)?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Falling
in
Love
(Is
Hard
on
the
Knees)">Falling
in
Love
(Is
Hard
on
the
Knees)</a>&quot;,
the
ballad
&quot;<a
href="/wiki/Hole_in_My_Soul?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Hole
in
My
Soul">Hole
in
My
Soul</a>&quot;,
and
the
crossover-pop
smash
&quot;<a
href="/wiki/Pink_(song)?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Pink
(song)">Pink</a>&quot;
(which
won
the
band
their
fourth
<a
href="/wiki/Grammy_Award?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Grammy
Award">Grammy
Award</a>
in
1999
in
the
<a
href="/wiki/Grammy_Award_for_Best_Rock_Performance_by_a_Duo_or_Group_with_Vocal?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Grammy
Award
for
Best
Rock
Performance
by
a
Duo
or
Group
with
Vocal">Best
Rock
Performance
by
a
Duo
or
Group
with
Vocal</a>
category).<sup
id="cite_ref-grammy_74-2"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-grammy-74"><span>[</span>74<span>]</span></a></sup>
It
was
followed
by
the
over
two-year-long
<a
href="/wiki/Nine_Lives_Tour?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Nine
Lives
Tour">Nine
Lives
Tour</a>,
which
was
plagued
by
problems
including
lead
singer
<a
href="/wiki/Steven_Tyler?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Steven
Tyler">Steven
Tyler</a>
injuring
his
leg
at
a
concert,<sup
id="cite_ref-102"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-102"><span>[</span>102<span>]</span></a></sup>
and
<a
href="/wiki/Joey_Kramer?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Joey
Kramer">Joey
Kramer</a>
suffering
second
degree
burns
when
his
car
caught
fire
at
a
gas
station.<sup
id="cite_ref-103"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-103"><span>[</span>103<span>]</span></a></sup></p>

<p>In
1998,
in
the
midst
of
setbacks
during
the
Nine
Lives
Tour,
the
band
released
the
single
&quot;<a
href="/wiki/I_Don%27t_Want_to_Miss_a_Thing?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="I
Don't
Want
to
Miss
a
Thing">I
Don't
Want
to
Miss
a
Thing</a>&quot;,
the
love
theme,
written
by
<a
href="/wiki/Diane_Warren?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Diane
Warren">Diane
Warren</a>
(with
uncredited
support
from
Joe
Perry),
for
the
1998
film
<i><a
href="/wiki/Armageddon_(1998_film)?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Armageddon
(1998
film)">Armageddon</a></i>,
starring
Steven
Tyler's
daughter
<a
href="/wiki/Liv_Tyler?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Liv
Tyler">Liv</a>.<sup
id="cite_ref-104"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-104"><span>[</span>104<span>]</span></a></sup>
The
song
became
Aerosmith's
first
and
only
number
1
single<sup
id="cite_ref-Aerosmith_Chart_Positions_46-11"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-Aerosmith_Chart_Positions-46"><span>[</span>46<span>]</span></a></sup>
when
it
debuted
at
the
top
position
on
the
<a
href="/wiki/Billboard_Hot_100?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Billboard
Hot
100"><i>Billboard</i>
Hot
100</a>
and
stayed
on
top
of
the
charts
for
four
weeks.<sup
id="cite_ref-Rock_on_the_Net_66-1"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-Rock_on_the_Net-66"><span>[</span>66<span>]</span></a></sup>
The
song
was
nominated
for
an
<a
href="/wiki/Academy_Award?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Academy
Award"
class="mw-redirect">Academy
Award</a>
in
1999.<sup
id="cite_ref-Academy_Awards_Database_105-0"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-Academy_Awards_Database-105"><span>[</span>105<span>]</span></a></sup>
The
song
helped
open
Aerosmith
up
to
a
new
generation<sup
id="cite_ref-106"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-106"><span>[</span>106<span>]</span></a></sup>
and
remains
a
slow-dance
staple.<sup
id="cite_ref-107"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-107"><span>[</span>107<span>]</span></a></sup>
1998
also
saw
the
release
of
the
double-live
album,
<i><a
href="/wiki/A_Little_South_of_Sanity?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="A
Little
South
of
Sanity">A
Little
South
of
Sanity</a></i>,
which
was
assembled
from
performances
on
the
Get
a
Grip
and
Nine
Lives
tours.<sup
id="cite_ref-108"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-108"><span>[</span>108<span>]</span></a></sup>
The
album
went
platinum
shortly
after
its
release.<sup
id="cite_ref-RIAA.C2.A0.E2.80.94_Searchable_Database_35-15"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-RIAA.C2.A0.E2.80.94_Searchable_Database-35"><span>[</span>35<span>]</span></a></sup>
The
band
continued
with
their
seemingly
neverending
world
tours
promoting
<i>Nine
Lives</i>
and
the
&quot;I
Don't
Want
to
Miss
a
Thing&quot;
single
well
into
1999.<sup
id="cite_ref-109"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-109"><span>[</span>109<span>]</span></a></sup></p>

ride,

<a

&quot;Walk

<h3><span
class="mw-headline"
id="Just_Push_Play.2C_O.2C_Yeah.21_and_Rocksimus_Maximus_.282001.E2.80.932003.29"><i>Just

<span

<p>The
band
entered
their
next
decade
by
performing
at
the
halftime

for
<a
href="/wiki/Super_Bowl_XXXV?qsrc=3044"

XXXV">Super

XXXV</a>,
in
January
2001,
along
with
pop
stars
<a
href="/wiki/%27N_Sync?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="'N

<a

<a

at

for

of
&quot;<a

<p>In

band
released

(Aerosmith

and

of

Push

(song)">title
track</a>
in
<a

commercials.<sup

They

to

<a

to

of
Fame

song

in

(&quot;Jaded&quot;).<sup

<a

<h3><span
class="mw-headline"

on
Bobo</i>,
<i>Rockin'
the
Joint</i>
and
<i>Devil's
Got
a
New
Disguise</i>
(2004â€“2006)</span>
<span
class="mw-editsection">[<a
href="/wiki?title=Aerosmith&amp;action=edit&amp;section=11"
title="Edit
section:
Honkin'
on
Bobo,

<p>Aerosmith's
long-promised<sup
id="cite_ref-Honkin.27_on_Bobo.C2.A0.E2.80.94_Review_123-0"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-Honkin.27_on_Bobo.C2.A0.E2.80.94_Review-123"><span>[</span>123<span>]</span></a></sup>
blues
album
<i><a
href="/wiki/Honkin%27_on_Bobo?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Honkin'
on
Bobo">Honkin'
on
Bobo</a></i>
was
released
in
2004.
This
was
a
return
to
the
band's
roots,
including
recording
the
album
in
live
sessions,
working
with
former
producer
<a
href="/wiki/Jack_Douglas_(record_producer)?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Jack
Douglas
(record
producer)">Jack
Douglas</a>,
and
laying
down
their
blues-rock
grit.<sup
id="cite_ref-Honkin.27_on_Bobo.C2.A0.E2.80.94_Review_123-1"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-Honkin.27_on_Bobo.C2.A0.E2.80.94_Review-123"><span>[</span>123<span>]</span></a></sup>
It
was
followed
by
a
live
DVD,
<i><a
href="/wiki/You_Gotta_Move_(video)?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="You
Gotta
Move
(video)">You
Gotta
Move</a></i>,
in
December
2004,<sup
id="cite_ref-allmusic_9-11"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-allmusic-9"><span>[</span>9<span>]</span></a></sup>
culled
from
performances
on
the
<a
href="/wiki/Honkin%27_on_Bobo_Tour?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Honkin'
on
Bobo
Tour">Honkin'
on
Bobo
Tour</a>.
&quot;Dream
On&quot;
was
also
featured
in
an
advertising
campaign
for
<a
href="/wiki/Buick?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Buick">Buick</a>
in
2004,
targeting
that
<a
href="/wiki/Marque?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Marque"
class="mw-redirect">marque</a>'s
market
which
is
now
composed
largely
of
people
who
were
teenagers
when
the
song
first
charted.<sup
id="cite_ref-124"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-124"><span>[</span>124<span>]</span></a></sup></p>








<p>2005
saw
<a
href="/wiki/Steven_Tyler?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Steven
Tyler">Steven
Tyler</a>
appear
in
the
film
<i><a
href="/wiki/Be_Cool?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Be
Cool">Be
Cool</a></i>.<sup
id="cite_ref-125"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-125"><span>[</span>125<span>]</span></a></sup>
<a
href="/wiki/Joe_Perry_(musician)?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Joe
Perry
(musician)">Joe
Perry</a>
released
his
<a
href="/wiki/Joe_Perry_(album)?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Joe
Perry
(album)">self-titled
solo
album</a>
that
same
year.<sup
id="cite_ref-126"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-126"><span>[</span>126<span>]</span></a></sup>
At
the
2006
Grammy
Awards,
he
was
nominated
for
Best
Rock
Instrumental
Performance
for
the
track
&quot;Mercy&quot;,<sup
id="cite_ref-127"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-127"><span>[</span>127<span>]</span></a></sup>
but
lost
to
<a
href="/wiki/Les_Paul?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Les
Paul">Les
Paul</a>.
In
October
2005,
Aerosmith
released
a
CD/DVD
<i><a
href="/wiki/Rockin%27_the_Joint?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Rockin'
the
Joint">Rockin'
the
Joint</a></i>.<sup
id="cite_ref-allmusic_9-12"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-allmusic-9"><span>[</span>9<span>]</span></a></sup>
The
band
hit
the
road
for
the
<a
href="/wiki/Rockin%27_the_Joint_Tour?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Rockin'
the
Joint
Tour">Rockin'
the
Joint
Tour</a>
on
October
30
with
<a
href="/wiki/Lenny_Kravitz?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Lenny
Kravitz">Lenny
Kravitz</a>
for
a
fall/winter
tour
of
arenas
in
the
largest
U.S.
markets.<sup
id="cite_ref-128"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-128"><span>[</span>128<span>]</span></a></sup>
The
band
planned
to
tour
with
<a
href="/wiki/Cheap_Trick?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Cheap
Trick">Cheap
Trick</a>
in
the
spring,
hitting
secondary
markets
in
the
U.S.<sup
id="cite_ref-129"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-129"><span>[</span>129<span>]</span></a></sup>
Almost
all
of
this
leg
of
the
tour
was
canceled,
however.
Dates
were
initially
canceled
one
by
one<sup
id="cite_ref-130"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-130"><span>[</span>130<span>]</span></a></sup>
until
March
22,
2006,
when
it
was
announced
that
lead
singer
Steven
Tyler
needed
throat
surgery,
and
the
remaining
dates
on
the
tour
were
subsequently
canceled.<sup
id="cite_ref-131"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-131"><span>[</span>131<span>]</span></a></sup></p>








<p>Aerosmith
commenced
recording
a
new
album
on
Armed
Forces
Day
2006.<sup
id="cite_ref-monstersandcritics_132-0"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-monstersandcritics-132"><span>[</span>132<span>]</span></a></sup>
Tyler
and
Perry
performed
with
the
<a
href="/wiki/Boston_Pops_Orchestra?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Boston
Pops
Orchestra">Boston
Pops
Orchestra</a>
for
their
annual
July
4
concert
on
the
Esplanade
in
2006,
a
milestone
as
it
was
the
first
major
event
or
performance
since
Steven
Tyler's
throat
surgery.<sup
id="cite_ref-133"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-133"><span>[</span>133<span>]</span></a></sup>
Around
this
time,
the
band
also
announced
that
they
would
embark
on
the
<a
href="/wiki/Route_of_All_Evil_Tour?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Route
of
All
Evil
Tour">Route
of
All
Evil
Tour</a>
with
<a
href="/wiki/M%C3%B6tley_Cr%C3%BCe?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="M&ouml;tley
Cr&uuml;e">M&ouml;tley
Cr&uuml;e</a>
in
late
2006.<sup
id="cite_ref-134"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-134"><span>[</span>134<span>]</span></a></sup>
On
August
24,
2006
it
was
announced
that
<a
href="/wiki/Tom_Hamilton_(musician)?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Tom
Hamilton
(musician)">Tom
Hamilton</a>
was
undergoing
treatment
for
<a
href="/wiki/Esophageal_cancer?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Esophageal
cancer">throat
cancer</a>.
In
order
to
make
a
full
recovery,
he
sat
out
much
of
the
Route
of
All
Evil
Tour
until
he
was
well
again.
Former
Joe
Perry
Project
bassist
<a
href="/wiki/David_Hull_(musician)?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="David
Hull
(musician)">David
Hull</a>
substituted
for
Hamilton
until
his
return.<sup
id="cite_ref-135"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-135"><span>[</span>135<span>]</span></a></sup>
On
September
5,
2006,
Aerosmith
kicked
off
the
<a
href="/wiki/Route_of_All_Evil_Tour?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Route
of
All
Evil
Tour">Route
of
All
Evil
Tour</a>
with
<a
href="/wiki/M%C3%B6tley_Cr%C3%BCe?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="M&ouml;tley
Cr&uuml;e">M&ouml;tley
Cr&uuml;e</a>
in
Columbus,
Ohio.
The
co-headlining
tour
took
both
bands
to
amphitheaters
across
North
America
through
November
24.
After
that,
a
select
few
arena
dates
were
added,
some
of
which
were
with
M&ouml;tley
Cr&uuml;e.
The
tour
ended
December
17.<sup
id="cite_ref-136"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-136"><span>[</span>136<span>]</span></a></sup></p>








<p>On
October
17,
2006,
the
compilation
album
<i><a
href="/wiki/Devil%27s_Got_a_New_Disguise:_The_Very_Best_of_Aerosmith?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Devil's
Got
a
New
Disguise:
The
Very
Best
of
Aerosmith">Devil's
Got
a
New
Disguise:
The
Very
Best
of
Aerosmith</a></i>
was
released.
The
album
contained
previous
hits
with
the
addition
of
two
new
songs,
&quot;<a
href="/wiki/Devil%27s_Got_a_New_Disguise_(song)?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Devil's
Got
a
New
Disguise
(song)">Devil's
Got
a
New
Disguise</a>&quot;
and
&quot;Sedona
Sunrise&quot;,
which
were
older
outtakes
re-recorded
for
the
album.<sup
id="cite_ref-137"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-137"><span>[</span>137<span>]</span></a></sup>
&quot;Devil's
Got
a
New
Disguise&quot;
peaked
at
number
15
on
the
<a
href="/wiki/Mainstream_Rock_Tracks?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Mainstream
Rock
Tracks"
class="mw-redirect">Mainstream
Rock
Tracks</a>
chart.<sup
id="cite_ref-Aerosmith_Chart_Positions_46-13"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-Aerosmith_Chart_Positions-46"><span>[</span>46<span>]</span></a></sup>
The
album
was
intended
to
fulfill
Aerosmith's
contract
with
Sony
and
tide
fans
over
until
the
band's
new
studio
album
was
released.<sup
id="cite_ref-138"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-138"><span>[</span>138<span>]</span></a></sup></p>








<h3><span
class="mw-headline"
id="Touring.2C_Guitar_Hero:_Aerosmith_and_unfinished_album_.282007.E2.80.932009.29">Touring,
<i>Guitar
Hero:
Aerosmith</i>
and
unfinished
album
(2007â€“2009)</span>
<span
class="mw-editsection">[<a
href="/wiki?title=Aerosmith&amp;action=edit&amp;section=12"
title="Edit
section:
Touring,
Guitar
Hero:
Aerosmith
and
unfinished
album
(2007â€“2009)">edit</a>]</span></h3>








<p>In
early
2007,
the
band
announced
<a
href="/wiki/Aerosmith_World_Tour_2007?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Aerosmith
World
Tour
2007">a
new
World
Tour</a>,
their
first
for
nearly
a
decade
to
include
dates
outside
North
America
or
Japan.<sup
id="cite_ref-139"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-139"><span>[</span>139<span>]</span></a></sup>
The
band
performed
at
London's
<a
href="/wiki/Hard_Rock_Cafe?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Hard
Rock
Cafe">Hard
Rock
Cafe</a>
in
February
2007
to
promote
their
European
tour
which
included
a
night
in
Hyde
Park
as
part
of
the
<a
href="/wiki/Hyde_Park_Calling?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Hyde
Park
Calling"
class="mw-redirect">Hyde
Park
Calling</a>
festival
sponsored
by
Hard
Rock
Cafe.<sup
id="cite_ref-140"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-140"><span>[</span>140<span>]</span></a></sup>
In
the
spring,
the
band
toured
Latin
America
to
sold-out
stadium
crowds.<sup
id="cite_ref-monstersandcritics_132-1"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-monstersandcritics-132"><span>[</span>132<span>]</span></a></sup>
In
the
summer,
the
band
toured
Europe,
performing
at
several
major
rock
festivals
and
visiting
some
countries
they
had
never
played
before.
Additionally,
the
band
played
in
Middle
East
countries
such
as
the
<a
href="/wiki/United_Arab_Emirates?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="United
Arab
Emirates">United
Arab
Emirates</a>
and
India
for
the
first
time.<sup
id="cite_ref-NewHampshire_7-1"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-NewHampshire-7"><span>[</span>7<span>]</span></a></sup>
The
band
also
played
a
few
select
dates
in
California
and
Canada
in
late
July.
One
such
date,
a
July
21
concert
in
<a
href="/wiki/Prince_Edward_Island?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Prince
Edward
Island">Prince
Edward
Island</a>,
was
the
largest
in
that
province's
history.<sup
id="cite_ref-141"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-141"><span>[</span>141<span>]</span></a></sup>
In
September,
the
band
performed
eight
dates
in
major
markets
in
Northeastern
North
America.
These
shows
were
opened
by
<a
href="/wiki/Joan_Jett?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Joan
Jett">Joan
Jett</a>.
The
band
also
played
a
private
gig
in
Hawaii.
A
public
show
in
<a
href="/wiki/Maui?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Maui">Maui</a>
was
canceled
for
logistical
reasons,<sup
id="cite_ref-142"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-142"><span>[</span>142<span>]</span></a></sup>
which
spurred
a
class
action
lawsuit
against
the
band.<sup
id="cite_ref-143"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-143"><span>[</span>143<span>]</span></a></sup>
In
April
2009,
Aerosmith
agreed
to
compensate
all
ticket
buyers
of
the
canceled
show
with
a
free
ticket
to
a
rescheduled
Maui
show
to
be
held
on
October
20,
2009,
along
with
reimbursements
of
all
out-of-pocket
expenses
related
to
the
show.<sup
id="cite_ref-144"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-144"><span>[</span>144<span>]</span></a></sup></p>








<p>On
November
1,
2007,
the
band
entered
the
studio
to
work
on
the
final
studio
album
of
their
current
contract
with
Sony.
At
the
time,
it
was
believed
that
the
album
would
include
both
re-recorded
tracks
left
off
previous
albums
as
well
as
brand
new
material.<sup
id="cite_ref-145"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-145"><span>[</span>145<span>]</span></a></sup>
In
an
interview,
guitarist
Joe
Perry
revealed
that
in
addition
to
creating
a
new
album,
the
band
was
working
closely
with
the
makers
of
the
<a
href="/wiki/Guitar_Hero_(series)?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Guitar
Hero
(series)"
class="mw-redirect"><i>Guitar
Hero</i>
series</a>
to
develop
<i><a
href="/wiki/Guitar_Hero:_Aerosmith?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Guitar
Hero:
Aerosmith">Guitar
Hero:
Aerosmith</a></i>,
a
video
game
dedicated
to
the
band's
music.<sup
id="cite_ref-146"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-146"><span>[</span>146<span>]</span></a></sup>
The
game
was
released
on
June
29,
2008
and
contains
many
of
their
most
popular
songs.<sup
id="cite_ref-147"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-147"><span>[</span>147<span>]</span></a></sup>
Steven
Tyler
announced
on
VH1
Classic
Radio
on
September
4,
2008
that
Aerosmith
intends
to
enter
the
studio
at
the
end
of
September
2008
to
complete
the
band's
<a
href="/wiki/Aerosmith%27s_fifteenth_studio_album?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Aerosmith's
fifteenth
studio
album"
class="mw-redirect">15th
studio
album</a>.
Tyler
also
confirmed
that
the
band
plans
to
begin
a
new
U.S.
tour
in
June
2009,
in
support
of
the
as-yet-untitled
album.
This
tour
was
supposed
to
be
preceded
by
a
concert
in
Venezuela
on
February
1,
2009.<sup
id="cite_ref-148"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-148"><span>[</span>148<span>]</span></a></sup>
However,
on
January
15,
2009,
Tyler
said
the
band
would
be
unable
to
play
the
gig
because
of
a
second
knee
injury
of
guitarist
Joe
Perry.
In
mid-February
2009,
it
was
announced
that
the
album
would
be
produced
by
the
famed
<a
href="/wiki/Brendan_O%27Brien_(music_producer)?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Brendan
O'Brien
(music
producer)"
class="mw-redirect">Brendan
Oâ€™Brien</a>
and
that
the
album
would
likely
be
recorded
live,
like
their
earlier
records.
Although
the
band
had
hoped
to
finish
the
album
before
<a
href="/wiki/Aerosmith/ZZ_Top_Tour?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Aerosmith/ZZ
Top
Tour">the
tour</a>
started
in
June
2009,<sup
id="cite_ref-149"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-149"><span>[</span>149<span>]</span></a></sup>
Perry
said
that
the
group
&quot;realized
there
wasn't
any
chance
of
getting
[the
album]
finished
before
we
hit
the
road
for
the
summer.&quot;
The
tour
featured
<a
href="/wiki/ZZ_Top?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="ZZ
Top">ZZ
Top</a>
as
the
opening
act
for
most
of
the
tour.<sup
id="cite_ref-150"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-150"><span>[</span>150<span>]</span></a></sup>
The
<a
href="/wiki/Aerosmith/ZZ_Top_Tour?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Aerosmith/ZZ
Top
Tour">Aerosmith/ZZ
Top
Tour</a>,
presented
by
<i>Guitar
Hero:
Aerosmith</i>,
was
officially
announced
and
the
first
dates
released
on
April
8,
2009.<sup
id="cite_ref-151"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-151"><span>[</span>151<span>]</span></a></sup></p>

<p>The
tour
was
slated
to
take
the
band
across
North
America
from
June
to
September
2009.<sup
id="cite_ref-152"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-152"><span>[</span>152<span>]</span></a></sup>
The
tour
featured
the
band
perform
nearly
all
of
the
songs
on
the
band's
1975
album
<i><a
href="/wiki/Toys_in_the_Attic_(album)?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Toys
in
the
Attic
(album)">Toys
in
the
Attic</a></i>
during
the
first
seven
dates
of
the
tour
and
also
featured
Joe
Perry
sing
lead
vocals
on
the
1976
<a
href="/wiki/Deep_cut?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Deep
cut">deep
cut</a>
&quot;Combination&quot;.
The
tour
was
plagued
with
several
health
problems,
however.
Guitarist
<a
href="/wiki/Brad_Whitford?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Brad
Whitford">Brad
Whitford</a>
had
to
sit
out
the
first
seven
dates
of
the
tour
in
order
to
recover
from
head
surgery,
after
injuring
his
head
getting
out
of
his
car.
On
June
28,
2009,
at
the
band's
seventh
show
of
the
tour
at
the
<a
href="/wiki/Mohegan_Sun_Arena?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Mohegan
Sun
Arena">Mohegan
Sun
Arena</a>
in
<a
href="/wiki/Uncasville,_Connecticut?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Uncasville,
Connecticut">Uncasville,
Connecticut</a>,
lead
singer
<a
href="/wiki/Steven_Tyler?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Steven
Tyler">Steven
Tyler</a>
injured
his
leg,
which
required
seven
shows
to
be
postponed.
As
soon
as
the
band
resumed
the
tour
on
July
15,
Whitford
returned
to
the
fold.
However,
<a
href="/wiki/Tom_Hamilton_(musician)?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Tom
Hamilton
(musician)">Tom
Hamilton</a>
had
to
depart
the
tour
in
order
to
recover
from
non-invasive
surgery.
On
August
5,
2009,
Tyler
was
rushed
to
the
hospital
after
falling
from
the
stage
at
a
concert
in
<a
href="/wiki/Sturgis,_South_Dakota?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Sturgis,
South
Dakota">Sturgis,
South
Dakota</a>.<sup
id="cite_ref-153"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-153"><span>[</span>153<span>]</span></a></sup>
He
was
helped
up
by
security
staff
and
taken
backstage,
before
guitarist
Joe
Perry
told
the
audience
the

was
over.
Tyler
was
airlifted
to
Rapid
City
Regional
Hospital,
where
he
received
treatment
for
head
and
neck
injuries
and
a
broken

In
the
wake
of
Tyler's
injuries,
the
band
was
forced
to
postpone
five
shows
in
Western
Canada.
On
August
14,
2009,
Aerosmith
announced
that
they
had
decided
to
cancel
the
rest
of
their
U.S.
tour
dates
with
ZZ
Top,
due
to
Tyler's

id="cite_ref-154"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-154"><span>[</span>154<span>]</span></a></sup><sup
id="cite_ref-155"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-155"><span>[</span>155<span>]</span></a></sup></p>








<p>In

of

completed

on

fifth

<i><a

(Joe

<a

released
his

<i>Hit
Hard</i>.
Perry's
solo
album
was
released
on
October
6,
2009.</p>








<p>After

<a

in
<a

<p>Tyler
pulled
out
of
a
planned
South
American
tour
at
the
end
of
2009
and
seemed
intent
on
pursuing
solo
projects,
including
his
autobiography
<i>Does
the
Noise
in
My
Head
Bother
You?</i>.
Tyler
told
<i>Classic
Rock
magazine</i>,
&quot;I
donâ€™t
know
what
I'm
doing
yet,
but
it's
definitely
going
to
be
something
Steven
Tyler:
working
on
the
brand
of
myself
â€“
Brand
Tyler.&quot;<sup
id="cite_ref-classicrockmagazine.com_156-0"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-classicrockmagazine.com-156"><span>[</span>156<span>]</span></a></sup>
Meanwhile,
guitarist
Joe
Perry
toured
the
United
States
at
the
end
of
2009,
and
Japan
and
the
UK
early
in
2010.<sup
id="cite_ref-classicrockmagazine.com_156-1"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-classicrockmagazine.com-156"><span>[</span>156<span>]</span></a></sup></p>








<p>In
November
2009,
Joe
Perry
stated
that
Tyler
had
not
been
in
contact
with
the
band
and
could
be
on
the
verge
of
quitting
Aerosmith.<sup
id="cite_ref-157"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-157"><span>[</span>157<span>]</span></a></sup>
Perry
stated
that
the
rest
of
the
group
was
&quot;looking
for
a
new
singer
to
work
with.&quot;<sup
id="cite_ref-BBCquit_158-0"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-BBCquit-158"><span>[</span>158<span>]</span></a></sup>
It
had
also
been
reported
that
singer
<a
href="/wiki/Lenny_Kravitz?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Lenny
Kravitz">Lenny
Kravitz</a>
had
been
approached
for
Steven
Tyler's
position,
which
he
then
declined.<sup
id="cite_ref-159"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-159"><span>[</span>159<span>]</span></a></sup></p>








<p>However,
despite
the
rumors
of
him
leaving
the
band,
Tyler
joined
The
Joe
Perry
Project
onstage
on
November
10,
2009
at
the
Fillmore
New
York
at
Irving
Plaza,
and
Tyler
and
Perry
performed
the
Aerosmith
single
&quot;<a
href="/wiki/Walk_This_Way?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Walk
This
Way">Walk
This
Way</a>&quot;
together.
According
to
sources
at
the
event,
Tyler
assured
the
crowd
that
he
was
&quot;not
quitting
Aerosmith&quot;.<sup
id="cite_ref-160"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-160"><span>[</span>160<span>]</span></a></sup><sup
id="cite_ref-161"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-161"><span>[</span>161<span>]</span></a></sup></p>








<p>On
December
22,
<i><a
href="/wiki/People_(magazine)?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="People
(magazine)">People</a></i>
magazine
reported
that
Tyler
had
entered
a
rehabilitation
facility
to
manage
his
addiction
to
painkillers,
brought
on
by
injuries
to
his
knees,
legs,
and

that
resulted
from
years
of
performing.
In
his

Tyler
said
he
is
grateful
for
the
support
he
is
receiving,
is
committed
to
getting
things
taken
care
of,
and
is
eager
to
get
back
on
stage
and
in
the
recording
studio
with
his
bandmates.<sup
id="cite_ref-162"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-162"><span>[</span>162<span>]</span></a></sup></p>








<p>On
January
20,
2010,
Perry
confirmed
the
band
were
about
to
audition
for
a
new
singer
to
replace
Tyler.<sup
id="cite_ref-163"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-163"><span>[</span>163<span>]</span></a></sup>
Perry

that

to

would
&quot;take

for

the

wanted
to

Perry
also
said
that
the

would
be

continue

Tyler
in

future

id="cite_ref-164"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-164"><span>[</span>164<span>]</span></a></sup>
In

and

a
&quot;cease

and

if

did

this

to
replace
Tyler.<sup
id="cite_ref-165"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-165"><span>[</span>165<span>]</span></a></sup></p>








<p>On
February
15,
2010,
it
was
announced
that
Aerosmith
were
to
headline
<a
href="/wiki/Download_Festival?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Download
Festival">Download
Festival</a>
at
<a
href="/wiki/Donington_Park?qsrc=3044"

id="cite_ref-166"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-166"><span>[</span>166<span>]</span></a></sup>
Steven
Tyler

It

<a

10

<a

title="S&ouml;lvesborg">S&ouml;lvesborg</a>.
During

&quot;the

On

for

<a

<p>Problems

<p>Around

â€“
&quot;I'm

id="cite_ref-174"
class="reference"><a

<p>While

Aerosmith

<i><a

that

will
probably
be
in
Los
Angeles,
where
<i>American
Idol</i>
is
headquartered,
and
a
world
tour
would
follow.<sup
id="cite_ref-177"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-177"><span>[</span>177<span>]</span></a></sup></p>

<p>In
a
November
2010
interview
reported
at
NME.com,
drummer
<a
href="/wiki/Joey_Kramer?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Joey
Kramer">Joey
Kramer</a>
confirmed
that
the
band
had
every
intention
to
finish
and
release
their
long-delayed
album
in
2011,
stating,
&quot;Really,
at
this
point
in
time,
the
only
thing
that's
going
to
stop
us
is
if
someone
out-and-out
dies.
Other
than
that,
we've
already
been
through
what
we've
been
through
and
stood
the
test
of
time.
What
else
is
there?&quot;<sup
id="cite_ref-178"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-178"><span>[</span>178<span>]</span></a></sup>
On
January
18,
2011,
Tyler
declared
that
&quot;Joe
(Perry)
has
got
some
licks
and
I've
got
a
bunch
of
songs
that
I've
written
for
solo
and/or
Aerosmith&quot;
and
the
band
would
start
prepping
the
album
that
week.<sup
id="cite_ref-179"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-179"><span>[</span>179<span>]</span></a></sup>
On
March
20,
2011,
Aerosmith
announced
a
new
greatest
hits
album,
<i><a
href="/wiki/Tough_Love:_Best_of_the_Ballads?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Tough
Love:
Best
of
the
Ballads">Tough
Love:
Best
of
the
Ballads</a></i>,
which
was
released
on
May
10,
2011.<sup
id="cite_ref-180"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-180"><span>[</span>180<span>]</span></a></sup>
On
May
14,
2011,
the
band
announced
a
tour
of
Latin
America
in
the
fall
of
2011.<sup
id="cite_ref-181"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-181"><span>[</span>181<span>]</span></a></sup>
In
June,
Joe
Perry
announced
that
the
band
is
going
to
meet
at
the
recording
studio
to
produce
the
next
album
of
the
band
in
July.
On
August
30,
it
was
announced
that
the
new
album
will
be
released
around
May
2012.
The
album
will
be
produced
by
<a
href="/wiki/Jack_Douglas_(record_producer)?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Jack
Douglas
(record
producer)">Jack
Douglas</a>,
who
produced
four
albums
for
the
band
in
the
1970s.<sup
id="cite_ref-182"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-182"><span>[</span>182<span>]</span></a></sup><sup
id="cite_ref-183"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-183"><span>[</span>183<span>]</span></a></sup>
Aerosmith
began
their
<a
href="/wiki/Back_On_the_Road_Tour?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Back
On
the
Road
Tour">fall
tour
of
Latin
America
and
Japan</a>
on
October
22
in
<a
href="/wiki/Lima,_Peru?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Lima,
Peru"
class="mw-redirect">Lima,
Peru</a>.
As
part
of
the
tour,
the
band
performed
in
<a
href="/wiki/Paraguay?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Paraguay">Paraguay</a>,
Panama,
and
<a
href="/wiki/Ecuador?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Ecuador">Ecuador</a>
for
the
first
time
in
their
careers.
Their
show
in
<a
href="/wiki/Asunci%C3%B3n,_Paraguay?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Asunci&oacute;n,
Paraguay"
class="mw-redirect">Asunci&oacute;n,
Paraguay</a>
was
postponed
a
day,
after
lead
singer
Steven
Tyler
sustained
facial
injuries
after
falling
in
his
hotel
room
shower,
due
to
a
bout
of
food
poisoning
that
dehydrated
him
and
caused
him
to
faint.<sup
id="cite_ref-184"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-184"><span>[</span>184<span>]</span></a></sup></p>








<p>On
March
11,
2012,
Aerosmith
was
featured
on
an
episode
of
<i><a
href="/wiki/60_Minutes?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="60
Minutes">60
Minutes</a></i>.
The
show
included
very
candid
interviews
with
the
band
members,
interspersed
with
live
performances
from
the
band's
2011
tour.
Some
of
the
comments
the
band
members
said
about
each
other
seemed
to
re-ignite
past
tensions
in
the
band.<sup
id="cite_ref-185"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-185"><span>[</span>185<span>]</span></a></sup>
However,
on
March
22,
Joe
Perry
surprised
Steven
Tyler
by
performing
&quot;<a
href="/wiki/Happy_Birthday_to_You?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Happy
Birthday
to
You">Happy
Birthday</a>&quot;
for
him
on
<i>American
Idol</i>,
as
an
early
birthday
present
for
Tyler.<sup
id="cite_ref-186"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-186"><span>[</span>186<span>]</span></a></sup>
On
March
26,
Aerosmith
announced
a
summer
tour
with
<a
href="/wiki/Cheap_Trick?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Cheap
Trick">Cheap
Trick</a>
entitled
the
&quot;<a
href="/wiki/Global_Warming_Tour?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Global
Warming
Tour">Global
Warming
Tour</a>&quot;.
On
May
23,
Aerosmith
debuted
their
new
single,
&quot;<a
href="/wiki/Legendary_Child?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Legendary
Child">Legendary
Child</a>&quot;,
on
the

of
<i><a
href="/wiki/American_Idol?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="American
Idol">American
Idol</a></i>.<sup
id="cite_ref-187"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-187"><span>[</span>187<span>]</span></a></sup><sup
id="cite_ref-188"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-188"><span>[</span>188<span>]</span></a></sup>
Shortly
after,
it
was
announced
that
their
fifteenth
studio
album,
<i><a
href="/wiki/Music_from_Another_Dimension!?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Music
from
Another
Dimension!">Music
from
Another
Dimension!</a></i>,
would
be
released
on
November
6,
2012.<sup
id="cite_ref-189"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-189"><span>[</span>189<span>]</span></a></sup>
On
May
30,
Aerosmith
and
Cheap
Trick
performed
for
<a
href="/wiki/Walmart?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Walmart">Walmart</a>
shareholders.<sup
id="cite_ref-190"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-190"><span>[</span>190<span>]</span></a></sup>
Aerosmith's
&quot;Global
Warming
Tour&quot;
began
June
16
in
Minneapolis
and
took
the
band
to
26
locations
across
North
America
through

12.<sup
id="cite_ref-191"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-191"><span>[</span>191<span>]</span></a></sup><sup
id="cite_ref-192"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-192"><span>[</span>192<span>]</span></a></sup>
The
band
hinted
that

would
continue
in

after

release.<sup
id="cite_ref-193"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-193"><span>[</span>193<span>]</span></a></sup>
On
August
22,
Aerosmith
released
two
singles
simultaneously,
the
rocker
&quot;<a
href="/wiki/Lover_Alot?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Lover
Alot">Lover
Alot</a>&quot;
and
the

&quot;<a
href="/wiki/What_Could_Have_Been_Love?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="What
Could
Have

Could
Have
Been

id="cite_ref-194"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-194"><span>[</span>194<span>]</span></a></sup>
On
September
22,
Aerosmith
performed
at
the
<a
href="/wiki/IHeartRadio?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="IHeartRadio">iHeartRadio</a>
music

in
<a

In

the

on
<i><a
href="/wiki/The_Late_Show_with_David_Letterman?qsrc=3044"

title="Today

and

and

on
<i>The

and
<i><a

In

and

performed
&quot;<a
href="/wiki/Dream_On_(Aerosmith_song)?qsrc=3044"

title="Dream

(Aerosmith

for

<i><a

Sandy:
Coming
Together">Hurricane

Together</a></i>
to
raise

for

that
struck
the
Northeastern
United
States.
On
November
5,
Aerosmith
performed
an
outdoor
concert
in
front
of
their
old
apartment
at
1325
Commonwealth
Avenue
in
Boston
to

and
their
Boston
roots.
<i>Music
from
Another
Dimension!</i>
was
released
on
November
6.
Two
days
later,
the
band
began
the
2nd
leg
of
their
Global
Warming
Tour,
which
took
the
band
to
14
North
American
locations
through
December
13.</p>








<p>On
January
21,
2013,
Aerosmith
released
&quot;<a
href="/wiki/Can%27t_Stop_Lovin%27_You_(Aerosmith_song)?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Can't
Stop
Lovin'
You
(Aerosmith
song)">Can't
Stop
Lovin'
You</a>&quot;
(featuring
<a
href="/wiki/Carrie_Underwood?qsrc=3044"

Underwood">Carrie
Underwood</a>)
as
the
fourth

from
<i>Music
from
Another
Dimension!</i>.<sup
id="cite_ref-All_Access_195-0"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-All_Access-195"><span>[</span>195<span>]</span></a></sup>
On
February
20,

was
announced
that
the

Steven
Tyler
and
Joe
Perry
would

<a

Two

was

that
the
duo
would
be

into

<a
href="/wiki/Songwriters_Hall_of_Fame?qsrc=3044"

<p>In
late
April
and
early
May
2013,
Aerosmith
extended
their
Global
Warming
Tour
to
Australia,
New
Zealand,
the
Philippines,
Indonesia,
and
Singapore.
This
marked
the
band's
first
performances
in
Australia
in
23
years,<sup
id="cite_ref-198"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-198"><span>[</span>198<span>]</span></a></sup>
and
the
band's
first-ever
performances
in
the
latter
four
countries.<sup
id="cite_ref-199"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-199"><span>[</span>199<span>]</span></a></sup><sup
id="cite_ref-200"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-200"><span>[</span>200<span>]</span></a></sup><sup
id="cite_ref-201"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-201"><span>[</span>201<span>]</span></a></sup>
Tom
Hamilton
had
to
miss
the
last
three
Australian
shows
due
to
illness;
David
Hull
filled
in
for
him.<sup
id="cite_ref-202"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-202"><span>[</span>202<span>]</span></a></sup>
On
May
5,
Aerosmith
cancelled
their
first-ever
performance
in
Indonesia
(scheduled
for
May
11)
due
to
safety
concerns;
the

threat
was
not
released.<sup
id="cite_ref-203"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-203"><span>[</span>203<span>]</span></a></sup>

30,

performed
as

&quot;Boston
Strong&quot;

for

<a
href="/wiki/Boston_Marathon_bombings?qsrc=3044"

title="Boston
Marathon
bombings">Boston
Marathon
bombings</a>.<sup
id="cite_ref-204"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-204"><span>[</span>204<span>]</span></a></sup>
The
band
also

at

<a
href="/wiki/Greenbrier_Classic?qsrc=3044"

four

<p>In

<h2><span
class="mw-headline"
id="Filmography_and_videography">Filmography
and
videography</span>
<span
class="mw-editsection">[<a
href="/wiki?title=Aerosmith&amp;action=edit&amp;section=17"
title="Edit
section:
Filmography
and
videography">edit</a>]</span></h2>








<div
class="rellink
relarticle
mainarticle">








Main
article:









<a
href="/wiki/Aerosmith_videography?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Aerosmith
videography">Aerosmith
videography</a>







</div>








<p>In
addition
to
recording
and
performing
music,
Aerosmith
has
also
been
involved
with
films,
television,
video
games,
and
music
videos.
In
1978,
the
band
starred
as
the
&quot;Future
Villain
Band&quot;
in
the
film
<i><a
href="/wiki/Sgt._Pepper%27s_Lonely_Hearts_Club_Band_(film)?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Sgt.
Pepper's
Lonely
Hearts
Club
Band
(film)">Sgt.
Pepper's
Lonely
Hearts
Club
Band</a></i>.
Later,
when
the
band
resurrected
itself
in
the
late
1980s
and
1990s,
Aerosmith
made
further
appearances,
including
the
&quot;<a
href="/wiki/Wayne%27s_World?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Wayne's
World">Wayne's
World</a>&quot;
sketch
on
<i><a
href="/wiki/Saturday_Night_Live?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Saturday
Night
Live">Saturday
Night
Live</a></i>
in
1990,
the
&quot;<a
href="/wiki/Flaming_Moe%27s?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Flaming
Moe's">Flaming
Moe's</a>&quot;
episode
of
<i><a
href="/wiki/The_Simpsons?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="The
Simpsons">The
Simpsons</a></i>
in
1991,
and
the
film
<i><a
href="/wiki/Wayne%27s_World_2?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Wayne's
World
2">Wayne's
World
2</a></i>
in
1993.<sup
id="cite_ref-IMDb_Aerosmith_210-0"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-IMDb_Aerosmith-210"><span>[</span>210<span>]</span></a></sup>
The
band
has
also
been
featured
in
the
2005
hit
comedy
<a
href="/wiki/Be_Cool?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Be
Cool">Be
Cool</a>,<sup
id="cite_ref-211"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-211"><span>[</span>211<span>]</span></a></sup>
starring
<a
href="/wiki/John_Travolta?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="John
Travolta">John
Travolta</a>,
<a
href="/wiki/Uma_Thurman?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Uma
Thurman">Uma
Thurman</a>,
<a
href="/wiki/Dwayne_%22The_Rock%22_Johnson?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Dwayne
&quot;The
Rock&quot;
Johnson"
class="mw-redirect">Dwayne
&quot;The
Rock&quot;
Johnson</a>,
<a
href="/wiki/Cedric_the_Entertainer?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Cedric
the
Entertainer">Cedric
the
Entertainer</a>
and
<a
href="/wiki/Vince_Vaughn?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Vince
Vaughn">Vince
Vaughn</a>.
<a
href="/wiki/Steven_Tyler?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Steven
Tyler">Steven
Tyler</a>
plays
a
major
role,
helping
Chili
Palmer
(<a
href="/wiki/John_Travolta?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="John
Travolta">Travolta</a>)
and
Edie
Athens
(<a
href="/wiki/Uma_Thurman?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Uma
Thurman">Thurman</a>)
bring
pop
music
star
Linda
Moon
(<a
href="/wiki/Christina_Milian?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Christina
Milian">Christina
Milian</a>)
into
the
limelight.</p>








<p>The
band
has
been
the
subject
of
several
video
games
including
<i><a
href="/wiki/Revolution_X?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Revolution
X">Revolution
X</a></i>
in
1994,
<i><a
href="/wiki/Quest_for_Fame?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Quest
for
Fame">Quest
for
Fame</a></i>
in
1995,
and
<i><a
href="/wiki/Guitar_Hero:_Aerosmith?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Guitar
Hero:
Aerosmith">Guitar
Hero:
Aerosmith</a></i>,
in
June
2008.<sup
id="cite_ref-IMDb_Aerosmith_210-1"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-IMDb_Aerosmith-210"><span>[</span>210<span>]</span></a></sup>
The
band
has
also
made
over
30
major
music
videos,<sup
id="cite_ref-212"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-212"><span>[</span>212<span>]</span></a></sup>
and
released
seven
home
videos
or
DVDs.<sup
id="cite_ref-213"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-213"><span>[</span>213<span>]</span></a></sup></p>

<h2><span
class="mw-headline"
id="Awards_and_achievements">Awards
and
achievements</span>
<span
class="mw-editsection">[<a
href="/wiki?title=Aerosmith&amp;action=edit&amp;section=19"
title="Edit
section:
Awards
and
achievements">edit</a>]</span></h2>








<div
class="rellink
relarticle
mainarticle">








Main
article:









<a
href="/wiki/List_of_awards_and_nominations_received_by_Aerosmith?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="List
of
awards
and
nominations
received
by
Aerosmith">List
of
awards
and
nominations
received
by
Aerosmith</a>







</div>








<p>Despite
Aerosmith's
popularity
and
success
in
the
1970s,
it
wasn't
until
their
comeback
in
the
late
1980s
and
1990s
that
they
started
winning
awards
and
major
recognition.
In
1987,
Aerosmith
won
the
<a
href="/wiki/Soul_Train_Music_Award_for_Best_Rap_%E2%80%93_Single?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Soul
Train
Music
Award
for
Best
Rap
â€“
Single">Soul
Train
Music
Award
for
Best
Rap
â€“
Single</a>
for
the
re-mix
of
&quot;<a
href="/wiki/Walk_This_Way?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Walk
This
Way">Walk
This
Way</a>&quot;
with
<a
href="/wiki/Run-D.M.C.?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Run-D.M.C."
class="mw-redirect">Run-D.M.C.</a>.
In
1990,
Aerosmith
won
their
first
<a
href="/wiki/Grammy?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Grammy"
class="mw-redirect">Grammy</a>
award,
for
<a
href="/wiki/Best_Rock_Performance_by_a_Duo_or_Group_with_Vocal?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Best
Rock
Performance
by
a
Duo
or
Group
with
Vocal"
class="mw-redirect">Best
Rock
Performance
by
a
Duo
or
Group
with
Vocal</a>,
and
went
on
to
win
a
total
of
four
such
awards
(all
of
them
in
the
1990s)
for
&quot;<a
href="/wiki/Janie%27s_Got_a_Gun?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Janie's
Got
a
Gun">Janie's
Got
a
Gun</a>&quot;,
&quot;<a
href="/wiki/Livin%27_on_the_Edge?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Livin'
on
the
Edge">Livin'
on
the
Edge</a>&quot;,
&quot;<a
href="/wiki/Crazy_(Aerosmith_song)?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Crazy
(Aerosmith
song)">Crazy</a>&quot;,
and
&quot;<a
href="/wiki/Pink_(song)?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Pink
(song)">Pink</a>&quot;.
Aerosmith
is
second
only
to
<a
href="/wiki/U2?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="U2">U2</a>
in
the
number
of
awards
won
in
that
category.<sup
id="cite_ref-grammy_74-3"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-grammy-74"><span>[</span>74<span>]</span></a></sup></p>








<p>In
addition,
Aerosmith's
music
videos
won
numerous
awards
throughout
the
1990s.
Aerosmith
ranks
as
the
ninth
most
successful
artist
(and
the
third
most
successful
group)
of
all-time
at
the
<a
href="/wiki/MTV_Video_Music_Awards?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="MTV
Video
Music
Awards"
class="mw-redirect">MTV
Video
Music
Awards</a>
(VMAs),
with
ten
such
awards
to
date.
Aerosmith
is
also
the
all-time
leader
in
the
categories
<a
href="/wiki/MTV_Video_Music_Award_for_Best_Rock_Video?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="MTV
Video
Music
Award
for
Best
Rock
Video">Best
Rock
Video</a>
(with
four
such
awards)
and
<a
href="/wiki/MTV_Video_Music_Award_%E2%80%93_Viewer%27s_Choice?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="MTV
Video
Music
Award
â€“
Viewer's
Choice">Viewer's
Choice</a>
(with
three
such
awards).
Aerosmith
has
also
won
once
each
in
the
categories
<a
href="/wiki/MTV_Video_Music_Award_for_Video_of_the_Year?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="MTV
Video
Music
Award
for
Video
of
the
Year">Video
of
the
Year</a>,
<a
href="/wiki/MTV_Video_Music_Award_for_Best_Group_Video?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="MTV
Video
Music
Award
for
Best
Group
Video">Best
Group
Video</a>,
and
<a
href="/wiki/MTV_Video_Music_Award_for_Best_Video_from_a_Film?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="MTV
Video
Music
Award
for
Best
Video
from
a
Film">Best
Video
from
a
Film</a>.
The
videos
for
which
Aerosmith
has
won
VMAs
are
&quot;Janie's
Got
a
Gun&quot;
(2
awards),
&quot;<a
href="/wiki/The_Other_Side_(Aerosmith_song)?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="The
Other
Side
(Aerosmith
song)">The
Other
Side</a>&quot;,
&quot;Livin'
on
the
Edge&quot;,
&quot;<a
href="/wiki/Cryin%27?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Cryin'">Cryin'</a>&quot;
(3
awards),
&quot;<a
href="/wiki/Falling_in_Love_(Is_Hard_on_the_Knees)?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Falling
in
Love
(Is
Hard
on
the
Knees)">Falling
in
Love
(Is
Hard
on
the
Knees)</a>&quot;,
&quot;Pink&quot;,
and
&quot;<a
href="/wiki/I_Don%27t_Want_to_Miss_a_Thing?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="I
Don't
Want
to
Miss
a
Thing">I
Don't
Want
to
Miss
a
Thing</a>&quot;.<sup
id="cite_ref-Rock_on_the_Net_66-3"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-Rock_on_the_Net-66"><span>[</span>66<span>]</span></a></sup></p>








<p>Over
the
course
of
their
career
(primarily
1990
and
after),
Aerosmith
has
also
collected
seven
<a
href="/wiki/American_Music_Awards?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="American
Music
Awards"
class="mw-redirect">American
Music
Awards</a>,
four
<a
href="/wiki/Billboard_Music_Awards?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Billboard
Music
Awards"
class="mw-redirect">Billboard
Music
Awards</a>,
two
<a
href="/wiki/People%27s_Choice_Awards?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="People's
Choice
Awards">People's
Choice
Awards</a>,
sixteen
<a
href="/wiki/Boston_Music_Awards?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Boston
Music
Awards">Boston
Music
Awards</a>,
and
numerous
other
awards
and
honors.<sup
id="cite_ref-Rock_on_the_Net_66-4"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-Rock_on_the_Net-66"><span>[</span>66<span>]</span></a></sup>
Some
of
the
high
accolades
Aerosmith
have
achieved
include
induction
into
Hollywood's
Rock
Walk
in
1990,
a
declaration
of
&quot;Aerosmith
Day&quot;
in
the
state
of
<a
href="/wiki/Massachusetts?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Massachusetts">Massachusetts</a>
by
then-Governor
<a
href="/wiki/William_Weld?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="William
Weld">William
Weld</a>
on
April
13,
1993,
induction
into
the
<a
href="/wiki/Rock_and_Roll_Hall_of_Fame?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Rock
and
Roll
Hall
of
Fame">Rock
and
Roll
Hall
of
Fame</a>
in

id="cite_ref-rockhall_52-2"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-rockhall-52"><span>[</span>52<span>]</span></a></sup>
and
being

with
the
<a
href="/wiki/MTV_Icon?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="MTV
Icon">mtvICON</a>
award
in
2002.<sup
id="cite_ref-MTV_Icon_121-1"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-MTV_Icon-121"><span>[</span>121<span>]</span></a></sup></p>








<p>In
the
fields
of
technology
and
video
games,
Aerosmith
has
achieved
several
feats.
In
1994,
Aerosmith
released
the
song
&quot;Head
First&quot;
on
the
CompuServe
online
service,
which
is
considered
to
be
the
first
full-length
commercial
product
available
online.
In
2008,
Aerosmith
became
the
first
artist
to
have
an
entire
<i><a
href="/wiki/Guitar_Hero_(series)?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Guitar
Hero
(series)"
class="mw-redirect">Guitar
Hero</a></i>
video
game
based
around
them
with
<i><a
href="/wiki/Guitar_Hero:_Aerosmith?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Guitar
Hero:
Aerosmith">Guitar
Hero:
Aerosmith</a></i>.</p>








<p>Aerosmith
also
holds
several
chart
and
album
sales
feats,
including
the
second
highest
number
of
number-one
singles
on
the
<a
href="/wiki/Mainstream_Rock_Tracks?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Mainstream
Rock
Tracks"
class="mw-redirect">Mainstream
Rock
Tracks</a>
chart
for
a
group
with
nine,<sup
id="cite_ref-Aerosmith_Chart_Positions_46-14"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-Aerosmith_Chart_Positions-46"><span>[</span>46<span>]</span></a></sup>
the
only
number
one
debut
on
the
<a
href="/wiki/Billboard_Hot_100?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Billboard
Hot
100"><i>Billboard</i>
Hot
100</a>
by
a
rock
group
with
&quot;I
Don't
Want
to
Miss
a
Thing&quot;,<sup
id="cite_ref-Guinness_World_Records.2C_page_206_214-0"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-Guinness_World_Records.2C_page_206-214"><span>[</span>214<span>]</span></a></sup>
the
most
<a
href="/wiki/RIAA_certification?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="RIAA
certification">gold</a>
albums
by
an
American
group,
and
are
tied
with
<a
href="/wiki/Van_Halen?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Van
Halen">Van
Halen</a>
for
the
most
<a
href="/wiki/RIAA_certification?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="RIAA
certification">multi-platinum</a>
albums
by
an
American
group.<sup
id="cite_ref-215"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-215"><span>[</span>215<span>]</span></a></sup>
From
the
<a
href="/wiki/Recording_Industry_Association_of_America?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Recording
Industry
Association
of
America">Recording
Industry
Association
of
America</a>,
Aerosmith
has
achieved
25
gold,
18
platinum,
and
12
multi-platinum
album
certifications,
in
addition
to
one
diamond
album
and
four
gold
singles.
Media
often
refer
to
Aerosmith,
who
have
sold
more
than
150
million
albums
worldwide
and
66.5
million
in
the
United
States,
as
the
best-selling
American
rock
band.</p>

Way</a>&quot;
at
number
34
on
their

of

type="text/javascript">




render_ads(false,
window['ad_config_bot']);





function
afc_match()
{








var
count
=
-1;








if(window['ad_config_top'])
{












count
=
window['ad_config_top'];








}









var
countBottom
=
0;








if(window['ad_config_bot'])
{












countBottom
=
window['ad_config_bot'];








}









if(window['backfillParam'])
{




























window['backfillParam']['pl_bmodn']
=
5;
























window['backfillParam']['pl_tnum']
=
count;












window['backfillParam']['pl_bnum']
=
countBottom;








}


































var
_matchUrl
=
"/afc-match?q=Aerosmith&page=1&ac=24&qid=A2357747C89E5E228B87238E0AA3C2D2&qsrc=121&dm=&qrt=2&lid="+
"&o=0&l=dir&oo=&cl=ca-aj-cat&ch=cx_ask_wiki,ad_dirN";





















_matchUrl+=
"&userip=76.78.3.114";




































_matchUrl+="&losid=a&locid=encw&lodid=us&loaid=a16";









var
location
=
window.location
+
"";








location
=
location.substring(7);








var
cutIdx
=
location.indexOf("/");








if
(location.indexOf(":")
>
-1)
{




















cutIdx
=
1
+
cutIdx
+
location.substring(cutIdx+1).indexOf("/");








}









var
urlPrefix
=
location.substring(0,
cutIdx);








_matchUrl
=
"http://"
+
urlPrefix
+
_matchUrl
+
"&afcec="
+
count
+
"&afcecb="
+
countBottom;








ajax_get(_matchUrl,
null,
null);




}





function
getXHR()
{








if
(window.XMLHttpRequest)
{












return
new
XMLHttpRequest();








}
else
if
(window.ActiveXObject)
{












try
{
















return
new
ActiveXObject("Msxml2.XMLHTTP");












}
catch
(e)
{
















try
{




















return
new
ActiveXObject("Microsoft.XMLHTTP");
















}
catch
(E)
{




















return
null;
















}












}








}








else
{












return
null;








}




}





function
ajax_get(url,
onsuccess,
onerror)
{








var
obj
=
getXHR();








if(obj)
{












obj.onreadystatechange
=
function()
{
















if(obj.readyState==4)
{




















if
(obj.status
==
200
&&
typeof(onsuccess)
==
"function")
{
























onsuccess(obj);




















}
else
if
(typeof(onerror)
==
"function")
{
























onerror(obj);




















}






















try
{
























delete
obj['onreadystatechange'];




















}
catch(e)
{}
















}












};












obj.open("GET",
url,
true,
"",
"");












obj.send(null);












return
obj;








}
else
{












if(onerror)
{
















onerror("Error
creating
XHR");












}
else
{
















a10.debug("Error
creating
XHR");












}












return
null;








}




}





afc_match();
